Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	2. And if you begin this, it is necessary, my friend, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first cauterizations, and for this reason greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	3. For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you should not attempt folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For there are many ways of people coming to treatments.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come from those who have so easily died with their disease due to the severity of its poison, and its greatness in maliciousness; and from these we must fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these I have seen you do the same, and say: "Wait, I am about to die"; and the disease is treacherous.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It only requires that you allow these who come to you who have this manner, but put more caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not trust entirely but wisely of the things which you are certain, and which you can have taken and lost; and use prognosis and indication in the cures of your diseases for the conversion of salus; and this will help to this good reputation, glory, and memory of longing.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Three things of great importance, Our Lords, give understanding and straightness to your hearts, and if you will seek the holy inspiration of her hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I have commanded this chapter in specifying it as a cauterization, according to what is before or after the cauterization, because you will find it more easily what you will do.
dou chief plein d’aigue	A full head of hair with age.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Scrapes that this disease comes from the child many times in the womb of the mother, and when it is pulled too hard on the head of the child; and never has it come from a cause that has been answered that they do not know.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease befall anyone but children, and in all cases that I have seen, death followed; and for this it seems to me that I should mention the work of the physician in part of the treatments.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I have seen a child with acute diarrhea, and the father fed him something every day until he could not bear it; and he thought it was the cause of death, and this moisture is assembled between the bone of the skull and the skull itself, from the ear to the skull; and the wounds are such that you should cut a large incision in the head, and so long as the moisture continues: and then the form of the spatulate:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more severe, and the abscess is larger, then I will make incisions in this manner, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is deep into the bone, and you see the commissures of each part of the chest overstretched, and the water gushes out when you press on it with your hand, and this has not been reported before: then it may be that you need to cut off the head III times according to this manner.
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After removing the dressings and powders, and anointing with wine and oil, and leaving it for five days; then remove the bandage, and treat the wound with compresses and poultices, and leave the shoulder evenly bound, and then rebandage the member as much as possible with dry cloth until the member is comfortable and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is to look at or open the large end of the abscess, and the rounded part; for it is never in front; never on the side; never on the back; and never on the side.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Make the opening of the abscess and the rounding of the wound according to what you have in your power; and be careful not to cut the artery; and come out with blood, if the patient dies by decompensation of blood and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of rumor.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When there is any disease called "cataract" in the eyes or ears, and the disease is ancient, and the cure of medicine does not help much, therefore it is necessary to cure it with cauterization if you cover the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is therefore necessary, if you can see the eyes, that the patient make a cut in his forehead; then rub the face with a sharp cloth as much as possible until the arteries are visible, then pull the cloth tight around the neck all over the cloth; then look to see if the wound is bleeding, and the blood from both sides are after the ears, and few are returned; then sign the legs with a pinch of a sharp spatula of II parts, as much as the cut comes near the bone, and that should be by the wide forehead.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, pinch the spatula of the artery and wrap it around, cutting as much as necessary, like two did to the bone.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	When the vein is pierced, if it does not stop bleeding continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open with pressure, then measure the quantity of blood that flows out, and then cut and put it back into the bone; and if it is six hours later, and by chance a little more or less, according to what the patient can bear, and the overflow of the artery, then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone without causing pain, then tighten the wound and tie it, and dress the wound as needed until it is healed.
de emigrainne	From migration
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When migration occurs, and the veins become thinner, due to moisture from tears and salts in the temples, and the face becomes pale and the same things happen, and it is treated with ways of medicinal cures and nothing benefits it, if we strick the arteries of the temples and cauterize, as we have experienced.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them if the patient makes the hair on his temples grow, and understands the artery that opens in the temple, because it opens well by its beating, and is quickly repaired; and if it is repaired, then draw the collar of the patient from the hair of others, then rub the neck with any rough hair, and rinse the neck with hot water as much as the artery appears clearly; then take the spatula of the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then gently burn the light leather until you feel the artery, then raise it to the top with pincers, and pull out as many stitches as possible from each part; and if the artery is subtle, then the thread at the tip of the uncinate, then the loop of that part according to the number of II chiefs.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not caught, then it will not be held at all.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And take out as much blood as possible, about VI c/, and if the artery is large, then it will be held with two strong silk threads of II c/. If the wound is deep, then the blood comes from the wound before the soaked cloth, and comes out in drops; then cut off the excess that is between the II liiens in that hour, and then, if you see, if the cauterization dou cautere cutellaire is as hard as the bone as long as the chiefs are caught; and this is the best work, if the patient has no fever and is of a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cauterization is helpful in ending the moisture: because it is of greater help to the moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arteries is necessary to fill the vein with soft cloth and place good stitches; and when you untie them, if you are careful with dry medicines that make char and tents, as long as it is healthy; and if without cutting the artery as much as you can, if you have to cauterize, or use your leather of vitrol and hold it in your hand that it is not smeared; and if you don't have this present, then put as much as the vein can bear that it is not frozen, and wash the vein with cold water as long as it can bear, and draw it out as it should be; and what is more difficult and lighter in extracting the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery sharp with two parts, but the cuts are well spaced to last longer without bleeding.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the wound is too tight, it holds less blood.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two incisions as much spice as possible, and then when you have heated the two holes, hold them red-hot until it glows against the bone, and close the vein in the two holes; and they should be separated between the two incisions since it is not a good thing to do this cauterization all over; and this is the form of the cauterization:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes descend from the veins that are stretched by the heat of the fire, and it does not profit at all with medicine as we see, and you see the face of the patient is distorted, and he feels pain in the front as if it were a convulsion; and they are thin and moist so that the paper seems to be cut, and the paper is torn and burned by the heat of the tears, if it has any use for this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	1. And they called it the "old bruise cure," and that is to make the patient take a remedy for this disease, which has long hair or front hair, then make three incisions or front equally according to the length of the forehead; and one of the incisions should be made in the middle of the forehead using a sharp knife, and the others should be made on either side of the forehead using scissors, and keep away from the arteries that are caused by the scissors, and separate your hand from the continuation of the mandibles, and each wound should have three doses of this remedy along the joints; and you will have a piece of sponge and moisten it with cloths for the sore to drain the blood of this disease, then cut the spatulum into two parts according to the form of the forehead.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	1. From the incision that is made in the temple to the second incision; and scorches all that is between the two furrows throughout the entire face that is exposed to the bone, then makes another part of the second incision, and then removes this sputum.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	1. If blood comes out in the first furrow with the instrument called "cultivator," and is very sharp on one side but soft on the other, do not sharpen it further, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	1. And the costeit (or coste) slicing towards the car (or track) of the bone, and the coste is soft against the bone, and the blood comes to the second furrow as much as it can to the car.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. And cut off all the veins that descend from the wound as much as the incision continues until it is closed, and then another part is made to fend off until the other defense; and then draw out the blood evenly, and express the leu for the blood taken; then put a piece of soft cotton in each fendure, and wrap them with fluffed linen cloth dipped in wine and oil, and keep the wound from drying out; and when the lien is removed, and apply large amounts of tincture of wormwood with olive oil, and other ointments such as balsamic ointment with rose oil, and others used for treating wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	The first sentence translates to: "He takes long and even hairs.
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	The second sentence translates to: "For when no cautery wound comes habitually, and you see the hairs thin and short, and the eye burned, and the papers burned; and the hair falls out, and there is great pain in the flesh, and the maiden grows pale; therefore, one should be careful of these accidents, as those materials and this cautery only cause many wounds, and this cure that it gives is if it is.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	The third sentence translates to: "And if you command the patient to shave his head, then make a deep cut along the front of his head, and another wide one in the opposite direction.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	1. And begins with the burning of the left temple to the right temple, and it is the incision into the bone; and remove your hand from the nerves of the temples that move in the jaw; and when the bone is exposed, if all the blood comes out onto a sponge, then dip between the two lips of the burning and put cotton on it, and sew with linen; then wrap the rough edges with wet vin and oil, and keep away from infection; when it is healed, if it comes to touch the bone as much as possible and begins to nauseate, then the cure of things that are exfoliative, which cause pain, follow.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In one way: take two parts of wheat flower, and eight parts of silk, and make a paste; and apply it to these wounds to heal them completely.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the ear's sweating
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that is on the ears is one of the four things: grains, or fat, or mineral piercing or similar thing as if made; or seeds, like hairs, feathers, and fleas; or something that flows, like hot water and vinegar and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When he presses on the ear hole or in another way of thing that does not fit well with the ear, and does not grow in the ear, if he puts the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the piercing, and there is no drop of violet oil or wax from it, then the extraction is performed; the patient groans due to the congestion, and their nose stinks when they exhale, and pieces of wool or lint are placed in the ear; the ear is soothed.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	This treatment is often used; and if it does not work, then the extraction is performed with forceps, as follows:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with the forceps, it is a success; if not, then the extraction is performed with gentle forceps, as follows: If it does not jump out, then make a small incision in the ear lobe and pull out the hair or the ear canal, and if it does not come out with the ear wax, then make another incision in the ear lobe and pull out the hair or the ear canal; then the extraction is complete, as it often comes out in this way; if it does not come out in this way, then take some gauze and put it on the ears, and do not use any instrument that could cause pain, and put a piece of cotton inside; then press the gauze against the piercing or whatever it is, and extract.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If she does not fall from all these things that we have said, if you hold her ear tightly even if it causes spasm and cramp; and the way of fending off is that you first clean the patient's head with warm water and then draw out the blood according to its strength, then place the patient's head between your hands and turn the ear towards the opposite side, and make a small prick at the root of the ear in the grease or where it depends; and the prick should be like a moon, as you move towards the hole, then the bone follows your power, and the saliva drips into your mouth; and the cure as soon as it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grainy and swells, then administer the extraction; and if it cannot be discharged, then apply a damp cloth gently according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision on that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not make the incision if you think the grain is moist from earwax, as many times as you need; then extract it with soft tweezers and gum, as we have said, if the extractions are healing.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the ear, therefore, if the patient has grain in the ear, the surgeon should use a cotton wad for cleaning and enlarge the ear with cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let's be cautious with that same ear or eye.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps for this, it's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If it doesn't, then take several piercings according to the length of your nail, and heat them slightly; and put the heating on one ear, and press on the other part, and firmly hold another piercing on the earhole; and continue making these holes one after another until the eye is completely out, and then it will jump all at once; and if you see, if it jumps, and take one of the ears, and the other one in fire as much as the more painful one is; then do another part of other piercings as much as the eye is completely out, until the eye is completely out, as we have said in the ear.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the tooth, if it is small, like a pea and similar, it is treated as we have said in the division; but if it is large, it can be felt, after the removal of forceps; and this is the lighter thing to do in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of the ears' rings, if you treat it as we have said in the division and after treating with distillations, and the care does not profit, then look at the ear with the sun: if there are no holes, if you take out the forceps subtly, and if there are, if you take the chain of this form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be tight and wide around.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And cut the hair more finely in the ear according to the amount of suffering the patient endures, then continue until the entire ear is shaved. Do this often as often as you can.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not yield to the scissors, then smooth it out with cotton wool as we have said in the incision of the verse; and if they do not become smooth as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have used in the decision of the verse, and you will find them or apply your oils and medicines in the ear through this instrument, regardless of the form it takes:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	1. And if it is of silver or gold, the ointment is to be applied to the piercings, and it should be distilled; and for pressing the distillation into the well-made silver instrument, and if you see take the feather and wrap it around the end of the point; then it will grease or juice, and whatever you see of your medicines in the gourd, and the gourd is in the ear; then blow the feather all over the cotton, and press your hand firmly until the oil is distilled or comes from the ear; and it will feel the poultice, and so is the distillations I pouch eschaufee at the fire as well as it can be distilled in the ear; and keep it not too cold, for the medicine will not be good if it is.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the ear's coldness
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without having some ear infection; and this very same thing happens due to the coldness of the ear, or from the cradle being too hard on the ear, and there are no signs of ear infection at any time if one cannot see; and never has there been a case of pertussis, and it is seen very well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes in front of the ear, if one cannot see it, is a sign of serious illness in many cases, and then it is necessary to put the ear that is sore with the salve; and look closely: if you see the exudation apparent, if the olive has completely this spumous substance of here, then the form is.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And so, and thoroughly clean both sides, if it does not hurt the ear; if the exfoliation is of char or cors of the ear, if you have subtle pincers, and a light cop, as long as that char is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the exfoliation is completely removed from the ear, if you take a soft, light razor and slightly burn the area, then you put on cors of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the exfoliation that the patient feels pain in the ear, gently pierce, and make sure not to hurt the ear nerves; then put a tent according to the large pus, and apply Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. Do nothing until the wound is healed, or take a tent and moisten it with hot rose water, and sprinkle it with powdered vitriol; and if you see the ear starting to come out, cover the tent with another soft tent made of oil-based and waxy candle, as long as the ear is still inside; then apply the remedy when it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	2. If the dislocation occurs, dip a sponge in cold water and wring it out, and place it on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the dislocation, which are treated with distillations.
de la char des papieres	Of the paper's folds
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the second line to translate:
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without dissection, if the cautery is a subtle cauterizing of the hair curler, and the cauterizer after the incision is not harmed; and they are repeatedly repaired, nothing grows from their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the grit
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come from papers the things that seem gritty in their form and hardness, and for this it is called "granule" disease, and it is a gathering of large moisture in the paper of its and other parts; the treatment is as follows: first, let the granule rest on both sides, and it is light to know; then make it wide, then burn each part slightly, then take with pincers, and cover.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	When you cannot perceive a piece of paper with your hand, if it does not cause any harm to the patient; and if the wound is large, if it can be stitched together, and cared for until it is healed; and if it is small, if it does not require much force, as the restoration will be done quickly and easily.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the snow is descending towards the ear to the part below, if reversed, and the snow is grasped with tweezers, and the paper is pressed from both sides; and if the paper is moved by incision, it causes no pain; and when the snow is covered, if the oily salty oil is lifted off, and the ear is cared for until the patient is healthy.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the hairs
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is engrained in the papers of the wicks, and this happens more often with fewer people, and it grieves their eyes, and they come to the candles at morning, and cannot look at the sun's light because the tears hurry to their eyes; and for this they lie on their sides, and sleep, and are covered in the wet paper that has been soaked by the oil and its appearance is covered in exinach.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press your hand on your two eyes and feel the exinach inside.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	1. And the manner of the incision is if the patient puts his head in your hand; then take a strip of linen and make a circle according to the quantity contained in each part, then put it on; and press with both hands, so that the exudate is assembled inside the circle; then make a mucous environment around the wound, cutting a large, flat slit, no larger than the wound you made at the incision site; and make the dressing as thick as you can see on the wound; and in other arrangements, exudate comes from the slit, according to the form of a small piece of greasy white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	1. Pluck out the thorn with all your might from the piece of bedding that is between your two cheeks, and turn your hands to the right and left as far as they can spread; and make sure you do not push it further into the gum, nor cause it to bleed.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	2. If the thorn does not open at the beginning of the gash, lightly open it as soon as it appears; then pull it out as we have said, and mend the cloth with thread and needles, and sew it to the lobe, and bind it tightly.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	3. And if such men who cut their hair and put on something to corrupt the moisture that is dried out.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the doctor, when he is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess comes to the limb, then the doctor should apply ointments that are gentle and suitable for the patient when he is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow on paper, and they are unnatural, and are watched, if they harm the eyes, and bring about diseases such as tears and mucus in the papers and albugine, until it is due to the destruction of the hairs; and the cure is done in four ways: either by burning together with fire, or by medicine according to what is before or in the chapter of cauterization, and is made either by cutting and stitching or by stitches and seams, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	1. It is necessary that you place the head of the patient in your hand, then turn the paper around in your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, then insert an awl into all the holes of the filament; and let the margin of the paper or the hair that comes from these hairs be on the part turned towards you, and turn it to the rasor; then make the edge of the paper, the hair straightened, in all the corners, from the largest to the smallest; then draw out the filament, and put a small piece of cloth and linen on the paper on the other side, then sew a figure on the paper according to the amount you see raised, like the thread of a needle, and it will be necessary that the figure is according to the quantity you see raised on the paper that is marked with your thumb.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	If a part of the body that is skilled in handling paper can hold a great quantity of paper according to its stiffness, then cut all the sheets along the lines you have written, starting with the largest loop as small as possible; and if one of the fringes near the natural hairs grows in length, then cut it at one of the two angles, then scrape off the root; then assemble the two lips at a stitch of a needle's eye on all the fine thread, and draw out the sinew; then sew the costure with an eyelet needle on all the fine thread, and draw out the suture, and make air the superfluity of the threads at the two corners for any gluans, if you see this done; and if not, then leave the stitch and the threads as they are for three or four days; then cure the wound with a costure of things that are dry and constricting, because the paper relieves the pain and assembly of the wound, but the costure is dead (as they say the ancient ones), and this is overrated; and if another way: and it is that you see the paper of a figure which is also like the fur of the marten, as we have said, at three or four oncines will follow the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then follow those who surpass in equal measure according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the nails, and the thing is not equal, then use a needle or a thread, and pull the hole; and take another thread of the same length for the great pain, and a smaller one for the little, and assemble the threads evenly; then gently bend your hand evenly, and gently sew all the leather where you have sewn it, as we have experienced, then stitch the corners of the wound by sewing, and treat it as soon as it is healthy; and if the suture comes to your incision, if the pain and swelling are assuaged; and never has the hair of the paper turned: if you use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching on both sides is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	1. The patient's treatment for rabid dogs is as follows: and if you follow this form: and then make the cords according to what I have said, and then make the cords by hand, and make them as long as the paper and the large pieces of the spatium are; and hold the ends where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly over the paper of the oil, and tighten the cords of the two parts; and leave no others, and the leather that is stretched will die and become rough and wrinkled, as long as it is on it.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed, and the wound has force, then the care until it is healthy; and when the wound is healed, and the paper is lifted, and no more hair is tied; and this is the form of the two knots that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The incisions are such that you will use a fine thread, and a skein of fine silk; then assemble the knots and gently insert them, and make the length of the threads as long as possible; then take another fine silk thread lightly, and insert the other knots; then put the needles in your mouth; and if the wound is healed, because it is a subtle wound and small, take the needle all through the chase at the root of the natural hair, and make it percure in the paper as much as you drag the natural hair; then pull out the hair until you reach the end of the chase, and cut in the chase the hair, if there are one or two or three or more; then pull out your hand as the hair comes all the way to the end of the chase with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	1. If the hunted one is treated and the hair does not grow with it, then if you trap the hunt with everything that you have ordered, as long as the hunt comes out with sharp pain and you see it through the vision of the oil; therefore, if you trap and cut the oil and leave it for two or three days, as long as the hair grows in its place and gives birth to the char on it; and if the hair is short, then accompany one long tail with natural curves, and take it with the one that you let go, as long as it is elongated and then tied.
de la porriture de l’oil	2. of the oil's nourishment
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, which is called "aleacrati" or the food comes in the oil, there are two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it comes through wounding, or cutting, or burning, and through similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of the surgery is to close it by cutting off the suture, and sucking out the leaks from it, and putting on linen tents, and leaving them as long as they are healthy; and only it is necessary to use in the cure of it things that dry and restrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease becomes worse than the first; but it works things that are softening, like fenugreek; and the heat of the water or the altee and the seed of lin are cooked, and all the oils are melted in none of them, and they wrap a tent around the cure.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure are if you guard that it does not sound like according to its form before; and these ovraiges that we have said no one has been worse than this disease, that it does not revive according to its form before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the horse that comes in the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is called "axacrati" is really called "axacrati", and it is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounding and burning and cauterization and things similar; and the view of the patient in the mirror is that if you look with a needle, if it has two threads, and the thread in the char, and it perceives the opposite arm as much as the other, so that the threads come in the shoulder; then the mirror is at the end of all the needles, and the cap is in the large spatule.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. And if the paper returns according to what it should be, that is good; but if not, then take a rasps and put it in the file, and turn the paper, and make as many cuts as the paper can bear; and let the heads of the angles of the incision you made be like those of a letter that has no "I griesche"; then do this cut, according to the quantity that your rasp cuts, of the same material that holds the paper, then smooth out the loose parts, and the cost of one thread of linen; then apply the cure that we have said about the mollifying medicines and ointments, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	The patient's illness comes from frostbite or freezing or cauterization, if it comes that you make a simple cut to remove the hair from the papers, and according to what is before; then between the two legs of a tent, as I have said; and it must be done according to the form of the disease, for it is different in shape, and the skilled masters arrange the instruments according to what will return to its natural form; and the illness itself, according to what it requires from the cut and stripping in more positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	It should be done on the paper.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this cauterization comes into contact with paper in a certain way, the paper sticks to the white of the oil and cannot perform its natural functions if you manage to poke the tip of a sharp razor blade through the paper and lift it up; and the tweezers, as long as you touch what is already wet in the subtle spumice, which is neither too much nor too little, so that the patient does not suffer from too much or too much oil, and your incision, which you scrape off that assembled one gently, if the paper regains its natural form; and it is healthy for all of that assembled part, and never once in the acidic cold water, and levigates it with cold sweet water and warm; then put a piece of linen between the paper and the oil, and put soft wool on top of the oil, and use dough and other soothing things until it is healthy.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the bone of the shoulder
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	There are two ways in which the bone of the shoulder can be: it is nervous and resembles hard sauce, and another that is not nervous but resembles frozen wax, when touched with iron and cooked with pincers, if it does not open; and both seem to end towards the great armor, and grow little by little until it covers all the eye and all the light and the movement of the bone.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the way of the incision if the patient places his head in the right position, then he operates on the bones; and gently take the paper with your hand, then pinch the bone with small forceps, and hold it at the end; then take a needle, and insert the horsehair, or sheephair, or beefhair, and the thread strong; and double the point of the needle a little and the thread passes through the bone, and perforate all the needle, and tie the bone with a thread and hold it at the end, and scrape all the hair from the costeit of the bone which holds the prunelle and the silk at the chief, then cut the remaining in the root of the arm as subtle and small forces as possible, and leave the natural or armor, so that by the incision does not come to the eyes' tears; and never has the bone stayed in the oncine only, and over time, as we have said; then it is all the spatumile soaked with coi ci is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the scars do not touch the charred skin and break it, and that the stitches are not perceived; then after the incision, a little oil is poured into the wound, and a piece of linen cloth is left there for a few days, and it is left until it is healthy again.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the unguent is not nervous, and you do not push the needle, and the uncini cannot enter, this appearance of a finger is often treated with various remedies; and I have often seen this in division, and if you see it coated, if you apply oil from the ointment of medicine, and take a light piece of thread according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And gently cut the nail, and if you see that it does not soften and the corner is pressing, then distill from your mouth into the oil made of lard and red wine and the oil will smoke until it touches the other part; then continue with another cut according to this same operation, until it is completely soft.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is nothing against you in the oil, as with a boil, then the milk, and first cure the boil until it is healthy, then continue the incision as before, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the arm is dark in the oil due to great exertion, and in cope a part and not the whole, that tears do not come; then it distills into the oil that is red and bitter, which is made by licking.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the cheek that was pricked by the thorn
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some men never prick their cheek, and they cut the thorn and tear the paper and twist the threads, and it looks like a rose of thorns; and if you do not do this, the patient's cheek will become infected, then you cut the ears, and take all those red hairs as close as possible to the skin, and hold them with force; then make the first cut, and continue cutting until the end, and keep the oil away from the wound; and this incision is like the one we said in the incision of the finger, and small forces of coi on the skin, if you follow this chapter after it has been demonstrated; and when the incision is completed and all the hair is cut, if you use olive oil or red wine and corrosive medicines, and put it on the wound with a piece of linen, so that it is assured of healing; and if it does not, and the without chaus runs over you, and you doubt healing, if leave the oil and cure the healing of things that soothe healing; then return to your wound as soon as it is safe, and then make many hairs that are cut in the oil by this appearance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary that you treat every weak point of the natural way; and of the accidental way, in fire; and do not force your hand into any of these ways until you see that the other member is affected by that way.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the hairs
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	These are red veins that are covered by the oil, and they touch the eye's way and weaken the oil for all time.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, the first thing you should look at is the oil, and since it is weak, there is no other disease but this oil; therefore, treat it in this way: instruct the patient to place his head on your hand, then stretch those veins throughout the entire body according to his wisdom, and make the veins subtle according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And so, cut the bone in degrees according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then, gently remove the bones one by one, and let the blood flow after each one, as long as you can see the bones coming out of the fat; and be careful not to cut the fat with sharp points of the spatula, and do this operation at noon before the sun, and work quickly in your operation so that you do not lose any bones; and when you have finished, distill the green and red oil into it to corrupt what is left behind.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot cut all of it in that hour, make a plaster with the oil of things that soothe the pain of the hairs, and leave some jors until the pain is soothed and the aposteme is secured, then resume according to this method as long as it is healthy; and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the oil fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	He asks if the fistula is called "arissati"; when it is cured by cauterization and according to the hot medicine as I have said before, and if it is not healed, then it must be operated on, and all the moisture that is in it should be removed, until the bone is discovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is discovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, if all the instruments of this case are made according to what is here described, and it is called "sharp chief," and should be made firm in the chief, and should not be cut too much like a lime when it is in this present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place the bone of the corrupted bone on the other, then twist it between your two hands, and press your hand for a short time until you feel that corruption is removed; and do this no more than once, then restore the bone with exfoliating medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the wound is found and not too deep, and the wound of the bowel is found and remains for 40 days, and it does not relieve or become infected, and no other remedy is found than to return the fistula to its place according to this form: then remove a second time from the bone with a knife and with medicines that cause ague, and if it opens after being closed in this form, and the head of the knife is at an angle of 3, and the fistula should be as thin as possible as you see, then.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	1. Then place the handle of the lancet on the shoulder bone, and move your hand away from the oil, then turn the entire forearm until it pierces the bone and feels the pain as if you are holding your hand on your neck; and then restore the dry medicine limb as I have shown you, and when the child is grown and hardened by the use of the lancet, if the matter is in the neck, it will be a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	2. of the issue of the oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	3. When the wound is completely open and there is no discharge from the bladder, and it does not cause any astringent or emollient, then you must apply the ointment to the wound and make sure it does not hurt by being too sharp; then put on linen made of acacia, aloe, frankincense, and starch, and then squeeze out the ointment onto cloths and bandages; if the bandages are not too wet, double each one into four, and then put one on top of the other according to the amount that the child has used; then squeeze out the ointment through a breadcloth made of fine threads, and resume the bandages until they are dry and do not cause any pain; then remove the bandages and let the ointment be dry for the night and the next day, and if it does not come loose, you can reapply the bandages after the night and the morning; if it does come loose, then you can see that the ointment is healing, which is good; but if not, then repeat the application of the ointment and the bandages as long as it remains healthy.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	A sudden tearing of the eyeball
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a sudden tearing occurs in the eyeball, it opens wide and shows thin paper like grains of resin; therefore, cover your eyes and cut off the root of the part that is most affected by the wound, then cut off another piece if there is a double thread in the part of the eyelid; and make sure, and leave the first piece according to its position; then cut off the double thread and take a part of the eyeball and pull it out well, then pull out the needle and put some ointment on it in a large amount of oil; and leave it as long as the threads cling to the eyeball, and treat the oil with comforting things until the wound is healed; and never again will the wound be restrained by any part of a circle of cloth, as long as it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.
