And if the hairs grow long and thick, then prick them with a subtle needle that comes from the oil, and draw out the moisture and the blood, and take care not to hurt; then pluck them as soon as they are healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the oil of the bow
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease, which is called "alcunnati," is not other than bows assembled in the oil, resembling acute descent; and it is not truly acute; and the appearance of the dislocation if you make sure that the patient lies on his back and right side, then take the chief between your hands of II parts, and pull as much as you see the bow coming to the end of your hairs; then it should be loose, and not shining, and you will see the symptoms as they come; and if it does not descend, say that it is acute, and if the dislocation comes from the bow is not assembled as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you place the patient's hand between your hands, then take the sharp spatula and make a cut along the corneo-limbal line as far as the continuation of the conjunctive with the limbal line. As the bow elongates, it distills in the cool, warm water meadow (honey), or cool and fenugreek is boiled in honey, then be cured by other means until it is healthy.
des aigues de l’oil	of the oil waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the appearances of the waters in the division, and when it comes to measuring; if according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	1. It is necessary that you place the oil between your hands, guided by the light of the sun, and make the healthy and tight hair long; then take the paper of the oil to your left hand, if the hairs are on the right side, or to your right hand if they are on the left; then take in your right hand, if the hairs are on the right side, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the hairs are on the left; then place the point of the instrument at the corona through the hole of a tooth in the blenchor of the oil at the smallest part of the limb; then push the instrument called "almagda" firmly, and twist your hand until it pierces the blenchor of the oil, and feel that almagda enters the empty space; and it is necessary that the measurement of the almagda hole be at the end of the spice that is on the prunes at the end of the nose; and this is the corona of the oil; if you see the bone in the paper for the clarity of the cornered skin, and then put the instrument where it belongs, or where the pain is, then compress one hole after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he feels pain now, if he sees the surgeon before him and the instrument in his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little while, if he feels pain again, open the second wound, insert the forceps with the instrument, and when it is firmly held and does not move, gently twist your hand a few times; then remove a piece of silk thread, and lift the oil from it.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply the oil-soaked cloth or linen that is finely ground into oil and a sufficient amount of vinegar, and tie it with the healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Yes, and we who are of our own kindred, put on cloths with a sufficient amount of vinegar.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the bone cannot enter the hole due to its hardness, because it has too many hard hairs, then you must first sharpen the instrument called "alberit", and its form is like this:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And by perforating only the conjunctive, and not too deeply, but make it subtle, then force the bone, as we have said; and at the end of the work, the patient will feel some pain in his shoulder, and he will sleep on his back in the dark room; and it should be done with all movements, and eat light foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and follow his disposition as much as possible; then he will leave this house in the same state as before the operation, and then you must see some things, and then put the bandage back on the following morning; but it is necessary that you do this in the eye of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you remove it, because the pain increases rapidly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When the dislocation occurs, you must slide your thumb forward on the seventh day, and address the one who reassures the dislocation; and when it is calmed, remove the eye and put it in your face or mouth to cover any joint, and be careful in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then you should leave the house quickly and quickly, and be careful that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And some came from Yrach who told us that in some places they made om almagda perciet, but I have not seen any of this in our land, nor have I ever heard of it in old books; and by chance, this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	These are the appearances of the forms of aemagd, because those who do not know them by sight; and these are truly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And be the head of this very subtlety, and the tail in three angles acute.
de la char sor le neis	of the cartilage that is the knee.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Never are born or grown any cartilages that are not of one kind, nor if there are any that seem to be like scorpions at the mouth of the thigh; and if they are of such a kind or have enlarged cartilage of fox color, and if they are of bone color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In those cartilages that are not enlarged and do not grow, it is necessary that you place the patient between your hands facing the sun; and operate on the nostrils, and grind the horn on those cartilages, and extract them; for if you do not hold them firmly with the tip of a very sharp and fine subtle spatula, as long as you feel that this cartilage is still intact.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If there is nothing else that can be done, and you examine all the surgical instruments lightly and subtly, if it does not cause any harm; and if you do not have an assistant, or if you are alone, and you cauterize as necessary and as quickly as possible, and make sure that all the bones are charred and not bleeding, then apply wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If you can operate, and moisture comes to the palace, and you know that it is healthy; and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, and you have charred bone in the bone, or the instruments cannot be cut: then it is necessary to tie the end of the linen thread around a large nail, and use your hands, and place the patient's head on it so that it can be held; and put the mouth on the child's nose, and let it breathe until it comes out of the mouth; and often make the child cry, and this is a light thing for those who see it; then hold the chin that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other hand holding the chin that comes through the mouth, and guide them one after the other until they are in place.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	1. Do whatever it takes to ensure the child understands that the cradle has been corrupted by the charm, then cut off the child's penis, clean the wound, and apply Egyptian ointment to the penis, then put it back in the cradle as best as possible; do this 3-4 more times until the ointment corrodes all that is left of the charm; then use a plaster of some sort for several days if necessary, and if the medicine is dry, use it; this is the form of the instrument used to purge the child's chest, or when distilled oils and medicines are used.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or gold, resembling a hanging lamp, like a dog, and it leads accordingly; and if you see, if a dog is closed, and it has flat ends to expel the blood; and it should have a handle at the head to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the heart the need
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times the head has been affected by a disease called "telul", which grows and becomes large, until it is seen when looked at; and for this you must first cut off the beginning, and then put on the bone all around, then put on the cautery or hot medicine; and if it is delayed as long as it is large, if it is hard, of a fleshy color, poor sensation: if it is not touched by iron because it is enchanted, for when it is cut once, no harm ever comes to the patient; and if the enchantments are many touches, not of fleshy color, you will see that it can be covered completely, if the patient is quiet and the mouth is open, and cure the patient of things that are dry and restrictive.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	It is said that when a solution for continuation comes from one of these cartilages, it does not last long and is only beneficial in some people.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that if no solution comes from any of these cartilages, and the wound is fresh at all its base; then it is best to close the lips with a thread, and treat the wound as soon as it is healed; and if the lips are already scarred on both sides, it is necessary that you remove all the parts of it that are healthy, and then close the lips with a thread, and extract it, and sprinkle dragon's blood powder on it, and burn incense; and put some pieces of emplaustre on the powder, and leave it as long as it does not stick to it, and treat the wound as soon as it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	1. The manner of sewing is as follows if you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in abdominal sewing; or by thread, as I have informed you.
des apostemes des levres	2. of the abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	3. that the lips of the abscesses are hard, resembling grains of sand, and smaller or larger; therefore, it is necessary to open the lips, and each tooth is extracted, and they are seized with pliers and held in each part; then use the leve after cutting with vitreol, as long as the mouth is not inflamed; and then the leve of ash, and cure the mouth of dry things as long as it is healthy.
de la char des gencives	Of the thigh of the knee
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times the thigh of the knee is cut, which is called "albulus"; if you can hold it with your fingers, and the cloth at its root, and leave the wound or the sanc; then put on the leu vitriole broiet, or other restraining and desiccating powders; and if the thigh returns after the incision, and many times it happens, if the cloth second time, and cauterize: if it does not return soon after the cautery; and these are the forms of the strumens.
des sordens	of the hernias
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	1. No times are assembled at the root of the teeth, the teeth are placed between the cheeks, the gums that are swollen and sharp; and no times is the black and yellow and crooked tooth, as long as corruption comes to the gum, and it becomes the crooked tooth; if it comes that you must place the tooth between your hands, and its roots should be in your holy, and open the teeth or the gums as much as possible, until nothing is left; and then make black and green, and yellow and other stains, as long as they are visible; and if it happens that this is in the first reason, it's good; but if not, then resume in the second day and tooth, as long as you have everything recovered; and notice that the teeth have the skill to different forms of dislocations according to what the patient demonstrates, because the raser that removes the teeth has other shapes than those that are removed between the teeth; and these forms and others are presented with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	1. It is necessary when you treat the patient's tooth pain that you delay until as much as possible, because it should not be done; for it is a substance that is highly juicy, therefore there is no excuse to delay.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	2. When the patient is constrained to eat, if you are certain about the tooth, then...
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	3. Many times the pain of the patient's tooth has passed, and it is certain that the tooth is clean, and the tooth is made to eat; and as long as the tooth is in, because we have already done this for these healthier ones, and when you are sure about the tooth, if it is necessary to cut off the tooth entirely, then make a small hole in the gum of all parts; then the mouth is your tool or has fine needles at the first point and then, as it is well anchored, it firmly fixes the needles; and the head of the tooth is placed in your healthy gums between your fingers, and the tooth is held so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After removing the tooth firmly with the forceps, and if it does not break, then take none of these instruments and pull it gently from each side slightly, and move it as you have done first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	If the teeth are perceived and extracted, then it is best to fill them with cloth; and if the extraction is done gently with needles, which does not break the tooth; and it is wise to overturn the gum over the tooth to clean the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And you should be very careful not to break it, and there will remain a part, and it returns to the patient through the malice of the root, causing greater pains than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	1. And you should know that what they do is not like what the ignorant healers do, who with their haste and their hardiness break the charm never, and they do not harm anyone that we have known; but they bring it once by the fever of this great disease, either by the roots that they cut, or by the broken charm, as often as we have wished; and when the wound is clean, wash the leg with wine or vinegar and salad oil; and if the sweat and blood come out, it often happens, if you use the ointment of vitriol; and if it does not work, then cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the wisdom teeth, or the first molars, are long and wide at their points and thick cheeks, which do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be of large gums if they do not break when pulled, and they should be made of good iron, and they should have teeth to hold onto.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth.
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root of the tooth breaks when pulled, if you must put the gum on the cotton-rolled end of the spoon for one or two hours.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the root is polished, put on the needles that are called "algefri," and even if the head looks like a beard; and they should be made as well as a lime and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out of all these pricks, then you must pull the plant completely out of the root, and insert the instrument called "athalise", which is also known as a "paling", and its shape is like this:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be sure it is large if it does not break the bone, and if the root jumps on this, it is good; if not, then use all the forceps, and the shapes come after like this:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you help with this instrument that has two prongs, and its shape is like this:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other forceps that are in front in the reason of the teeth, and this instrument which seems like large thorns, and its shape is like this:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	1. And so it should be that it cannot break, and it is sharpened like the teeth of a saw; and thus with other tools, which are not as good; and the surgeons make their instruments subtle by themselves, according to what their hands and the disease demonstrate, because they have some diseases or the ancients did not teach any instrument for the diversity of things and they do not break due to charret or other bones, or they porridge, if it seeks estruments that I have said, and I help with gestures, of which the form is:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-held to hold the bone, so it does not slip, but can hold and rest; and then restore the body of the medicine fitting for this, and if there is in the bone a fissure, and it is small, then all this instrument is enough:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears to not fit the natural body, and its form is misshapen, and at the same time in women with pubic hair, if it comes out after the tooth, and it is not right in the gum, and it cannot be sewn or woven: then cut it; and if it is with the tooth, if it takes this instrument whose form is like the small beak, and is of iron, and is sharp in its head:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And quickly and quickly with the hands, for the pain of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears to be like this, then you can limp, if the leg of a part of the leg like this is formed:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is like the leg of a part of the leg like this is made; and in the leg the tooth little by little with the hands lightly, if it does not move at all, then the end is completely straight, and the tongue is too thin and it crops the tongue, if it can limp the harsh one as much as possible, if it does not crop the tongue does not corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth loosen by pressure or chewing, and the patient cannot press on them because they hurt, and you treat them with restricting medicines, and it does not work; if they can be restrained by a golden thread, for the silver wire becomes green and rotten, but the gold does not move at all; and the thread should not be too thick or too thin, according to the amount of space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth, take a golden thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then put the threads between the rotten teeth, as long as you see improvement in the healthy tooth on the other side; then resume covering the wound on the part where you cut, and gently and skillfully pull your hand, so that it does not move at all; and if the root of the tooth is loose, so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then stitch the head of the thread to a needle, and sew it, and place it between the healthy tooth, and put it in so that it does not bend the tongue; and then leave it tight as much as possible, and if it loosens, or the thread breaks, if another thread is used; if it remains tight and serves for all its teeth, and is the shape of the roots of the two healthy teeth and the two roots of the two wisdom teeth, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is loose, if it is reset in its place, tighten it gradually, as we have said; and do not let it become too tight that it becomes uncomfortable and breaks, and never forms a shape like a bone of a moose tooth, and it is placed where it should be, and the tension is tightened as we have said, and remains tight and serves for all its teeth.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	The first line of the text translates to: "Of the tongue's root, the line".
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No occasion is known to have occurred where the tongue or its roots come out of the mouth, unless by accident of injury; and the language is such that one can make the mouth of the midwife, and it should be in good condition, and the tongue is dislodged from its place, and if it becomes hard or out, and this is due to pain, if the tooth pierces or cuts, and it is due to pain, then the large end should be covered with a piece of cloth; and make sure that the tongue does not become too hot, for the artery that is outside; and when you have done it, if the lip is red and swollen, or cold, then put the tongue under a tent of linen; and the woman should be examined every night, that the midwife may be able to suture.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the dislocation occurs, if they quickly set the bone with vitreol, and if it does not come out, if the cauterization is done at the slow burning cautery, which is suitable for this, then the care of another kind as soon as it is healthy.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see that it is red or black or hard, if the patient does not feel it, if it is not touched, because it is gangrene; and if it is declining into a blenchor, and it is moist, if it sweats the onion, and it is made with a subtle sponge, and the exudation from both sides; and if it does not come out of your body, if you set it with vitreol as soon as it is inflamed, then return to your body as soon as you have dealt with everything; then lift the limb with ease and with a bandage, and the care of other treatments as soon as it is healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses of the chin
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Never comes a chin abscess called "godath", and they are properly the second mandibles, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, if they are not healthy, then hold them: if they are sore, small in size and of a fusse color, and not red with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, but not with iron, then for the recovery of blood; but let it be as long as it is dead, and then you will leave it, or it will break by itself; and if it is a blainche color and the root is subtle, and you have prepared the instrument with copper, but first look at whether the chalz apostemes are resting and are soothed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then place the patient facing the sun, and their head should be in good condition. The operation of the mouth and the tongue between the hands, and press the lingua as far as all the instrument, whether it is silver or golden subtle also like some counters:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue all the way to this instrument, and see the incision, if you take the tweezers and the finger in the ginger, and draw it further than you can; and take no thing from the tools with it, then the hook to the instrument, whether it is silver or golden subtle also like some counters; and all the chief are corbé, and one place another, and are very sharp, and is made of iron inde or of adamant:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you have needles, then the form is as follows:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let the incision be on one side and the other part named; and when you have cut one of the hams, if you cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision, heat the instrument with hot, hot, and acidic water, and the sutures will come loose if the instrument is heated or if burns from green pomegranates are treated, or if wounds from mirts are treated, and similar things, as long as the mouth is not inflamed; then the cure is performed until it is healthy; and never have any other sutures born in the mouth except the two hams, if they are cut like the two hams.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with a wound that did not allow her to swallow, which is to say a small-sensored wound; and she had closed most of the throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the conduit that was stopped up, and could not drink or urinate, and died if she delayed for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the wound was so high that it had been stitched with two stitches through the two holes.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I made a cut in the other hole, and took out a large portion of bowel; then I made another incision in the other wound and opened the mouth and pressed on the tongue; after making the cut in these wounds and taking out a piece, there was only a little blood; and then the woman vomited from the throat, and began to drink water and then wine, and continued to treat the wound with long tenths; the wound closed up, filled the socket that I had made, so that it did not hurt much; therefore I closed it and cauterized the throat: afterwards it did not swell; and I left these parts, and only God will do for me afterward.
de l’uve	Of the urethra
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the urethra is drawn out of the urethra, and it is long and straight, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is very large and rounded, it is called "urethra".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When the urethra is treated as we have described in the division, and the treatment does not help, you see that the cauterization marks are soothing and subtle, and it is appropriate to cut it; and that which is rounded and not long; and it is bloody or red or black, and it is appropriate to avoid the incision of the knife.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary therefore, as you see, according to the method I have described, of the patient's gallbladder and length, that you place the patient facing the sun, and press the tongue on the instrument we made note of earlier; then make a cut in the eye, and draw it out, and close it with the two stitches I mentioned in the incision of the two eyes.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut too much beyond the natural termination; for if you cut more, you will grieve the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we said in the incision of the two eyes, and cure as long as it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient suffers from cold pain, then you must use an engine for the fire cautery of the affected part.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of burning is sharp when it is hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the patient places his head on your shoulder and then presses his tongue onto the instrument we have called the fire cautery in this chapter, and confines it with sharp, hot iron, so that it is neither too thick nor too thin; and then uses the angle of this instrument, then its form is:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient has a lock of hair or puts medicine in his mouth, like the mouthfuls of a child, and places the instrument at the entire medicine on the eye; and the patient is grimacing on his chest, if the saliva and muskilage come from his mouth with the medicine given, if it does not descend to the throat and jaw, then hold your hand on all the medicine and press on the eye, as much as you see the pain and the medicine's bitterness is soothed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the cotton in the hair ribbon as much as the cotton dries on the eye; and do this often until the cauterization is perfect, then leave it to dry, and after four or five hours or days, if you have skill in renewing the medicine cauterization, if it resumes, and after cauterizing the discharge into the eye, wrap it in wool, and clean what is outside of the medicine; and be washed with cold water, and be cured with gargles as much as possible.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This remedy is safer than incision alone, only cauterization; if it is treated with fumigation in this way, take vinegar, oil, oregano, rosemary, chamomile, and all or none of these herbs in one pot, and mix them together, and boil; the mixture can be well glued with strong earth, and the pot should have the instrument made according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it can be of silver or gold, and one of the points of the sharp instrument is put in the patient's mouth as much as the vapor rises up the urethra through the urethral opening, as long as the urethra is mortified; afterwards, it often happens again, as long as the urethra dries out, and make sure you do not do this at the beginning of the onset of gangrene, because more things come; and do not make this cut only when the decline of gangrene begins.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a needle and make a hole in the cheek with a thorn, for the thorn will not hurt the mouth too much; because the thorn does not pierce the gum and cause pain to the mouth, and that is a good cure together.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it has happened in the throat with a bone or a fish spine, or nothing at all; if it comes then that you must see what you can, and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see the thing; and whatever does not open and is stuck in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit unless the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance if it is found by vomiting; or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a crumb of dry bread; and then glue it to the sponge and then stretch it; and when it reaches the mouth, if it slips, and then draw it out; and if it does not come from what we have said, then take the instrument of plucking according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	Here comes the translation:
de la sansue de la gorge	Of the dislocation of the jaw
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	There is no such thing as medicine for the dislocation of the jaw, as I said in the division, by the use of medicines; and when it does not help at all, then look at the mouth of the patient towards the sun, then press the tongue with the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the dislocation, if it has all small bones, or thin nails that are worth this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if it is not worth anything, then take a hair of your head, and pull on the jaw of the patient, then pull or cut with the hair and make it often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And the patient's skin is marked with fever all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then I see cold fever, and I open the mouth, and the throat feels dry, and it moves often; and if quickly like the naked person feels the fever, then it is.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not have fever as we have said, if the patient is subfuming with asafetida, at the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will feel relieved.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of the fumigation if you see that you have or it has charcoal, and it is covered with a covering in a certain environment, and in the room the patient's head is placed on the instrument; then your fumigation is done, and the patient puts the end of the cainne in his mouth, and closes the mouth, so that the smoke does not enter, but goes to the naked person; and the naked person will now be feverish, and if it does not have fever again, renew the fumigation many times; and the patient suffers from thirst, and drinks salty and acidic things, and does not drink any water; and then he performs this service as it should be done by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument used to treat the wound, if it is the case, resembles tacks corbes when seen, like a beak of surgery, and has sharpness like lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot let go; and thus the form is:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of the stitches
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	The appearances of the stitches are, according to what remembers that they come after one another in this book, and are different in perforation and size; and there are two ways in which one is in its own appearance itself, and due to it being moist.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is if the bones are broken or they are in the carriage.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	However, the wounds of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the wounds caused by the cart are different from those that come from joints, and each person will have their own judgment in the matter.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if in wounds we cannot perceive, as long as the bowel is alive according to its completion; and if in such cases it is necessary to perceive when they are believed to be dead, and do not die according to their completion, like wounds that are from dislocations.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when wounds come from dislocations, and they are left as long as they are soft and tender, by chance if the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, because this is due to contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	For the incision, if it pierces the principal member, and you delay the perforation as long as possible before it is dead, it will harm the principal member; or it is due to the foundation, if the hole is not made until it is dead; and one must only cut the incision thought to be completed with digestion, as the one that is due to the foundation, it will not bleed much, and will be long-lasting and will form a fistula; and cannot heal in a great period of time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	It is necessary that you clean the wound of the incision made by the death of the principal member, according to its completion, and when the pain is eased, when the fever subsides, when the pain and bruising are reduced, and when there is debate and ague in the principal member, and other signs; and it is necessary that you sew the wound or more dependent on the incision, and where it was opened; and that the wound be long and wide, and if the incision is made with hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all of them equal or without a suture.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that prick, according to the member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the body, if it is necessary to leave the puncture as soon as it is confirmed in digestion completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you prick before this, and the heart comes out of it, and it is painful to defecate; and by chance they harden the lips and become flat from it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is no abscess that is pricked according to the size of the heart, according to what the member can endure.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you treat small abscesses, small pustules; and in large abscesses, large pustules, and many scabs according to the appearance of the abscess; and if in such abscesses or they come out with the cheek, and close; when it becomes as I describe it, and is worn out, then it is necessary to do it in the same way as making buboes: and if in such ones that are cut at three angles, and in such ones that are cut like the thorn of a myrtle, like abscesses of anger; and if in such ones or they make a small cut, and other sizes and appearances are covered.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	For the one who does not have a head, if it is a superficial abscess like an abscess, it is necessary to percussion plainly; and when the abscess is large, and it has entered the bone, and it is pierced, if not all the bone is torn in that hour, but only a part of it, then the abscess stops and goes to the other side, and no foreign body is left; this is done repeatedly many times until the bone is entirely filled; at the same time, if the patient is weak in willpower, or a woman carries, or children are small, or old men have decrepit bones.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the expectations have never happened once with the end of the bowels, by chance died the patient, and you do not know.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you perceive your abscess, if the wound is large, look at the size of the abscess; if it is a small one, use linen or cotton bandages; if it is large abscesses and has purulent matter, then wrap each in a bandage so that one covers the other; if you have cut a part of leather in the abscess and it has grown out, then fill it with fine cloth or rough fabric from rags, and sew it to the bone as soon as possible, then the bone, and the care of ointment as long as it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if the dislocation occurs in the shoulder, if it is not promptly treated with cold and wet cloths and gentle handling, and does not improve, it may lead to further displacement.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation persists, if it is not promptly treated with government and care, and the powders I mentioned in my hands in this book are applied, and if it is not relieved, then you should make compresses and bandages wet with vinegar and olive oil; and if it is like this, and the dislocation is severe, then it is necessary to make compresses and bandages wet with cold and olive oil, or with wine and oil, as often as necessary, according to what we have said; and then remove the aposteme and the wound, and the cure, as it is necessary, until it is healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this comes to understanding in the treatment of abscesses: or you have said what one must do before the treatment of abscesses, and now this chapter.
des soros	and desiccated bones.
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When many abscesses come and are like us in their appearance, just as the grape of a vine, and they have similarities.

If they are fat and soft or moist, just like pigs; and if they are hard and rough to cut, and there is no doubt that the patient will not endure it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the cuts if you try on all the instruments that are called "enterotome", of which the form comes after, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they are made longer by suspension.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then repeat the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the wound, until you see that it does not hurt at night; then treat the wound with ointment according to what is suitable, until it is healthy.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the stitch holds tight, then it is not long; and if the thread follows this form, it should be long; and it will burn your bones, and scorch all parts, and put all your care into drawing the wound closed or opening it; and if the blood flows against it, do as I have said after this.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And if you make an aperture when it is purulent, and cut and care for it as I have said.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the opening is made around the purulent aperture and moist, if it is lighter, because there are few stains.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if any of these apertures or heads have no moisture, and these were made by me or another woman of old; and you find the aperture as a sharp, spiny, bluish piercing, unable to be broken; and if none was made, it would have been as good as a piercing.
