In other cases, when a wound is present or chief, it is better that those who come for the children and the roots of the ears, open it as soon as possible to the most dependent part of the ear, to muzzle the bow; and treat the wound as necessary.
des scrophules	of scrophules
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	There are often cases of dislocation at the collarbone, and loosening of the clasps, and gnawing, and never have they come from another part or been torn, and they are always crooked, and one is crushed by the other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrophule is properly situated on its side, as if the wound and dislocation at the chief were not present; and the appearances of these scrophules are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	It is necessary for you to have tools that contain moisture, and if they are malicious and do not want to follow the health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	If you see the bone in good position at the point, and it is like the color of the corse, and quiet in every part and not rough as the veins or the artery or the conduct, and is not rough; if it comes that you cut it with a knife, and burn in every part, and the lips of the teeth are rough as the nails, then you can do it, as we have said in the apostles; and it is easy and quick, and you are sure that you will not cut the nerve or the vein, and will not be rough, that the hands will not break, and will not see too soon, that you will not cut more than you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you prick the vein or artery, and it does not let you bleed, then put vitrol beads or any powders that remain sand in the wound, and pull the wound; and leave it until the inflammation is soothed and the wound is softened, and it begins to ooze.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is healed, if it returns to its place, as soon as you have completed it; then wait for your time to indicate if it does not have any small scars, such as cuts and scratches.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if the scar is large, then it is only necessary to cut out that scar at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and leave it hanging without harm; then apply the wound with soft cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then the cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cover the entire wound, if you manage to gather the two lips of the wound, and hold them now, then there will be no excess because of the size of the scrophule.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you understand how to cover the root of it and draw out, and cut as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scars that have superfluity, perforate them if they are closed or open; and the perforation is done as we have said, depending on the one before mentioned, then use ointments and similar things, so that it does not corrupt what has been cut off; and when the wound is well healed, if the cure of ointment is charged with heat, until it is healthy.
de squinance	Of the glabella
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and talked about the tailoring of the neck; but I have never seen anyone do this in our time, and this is the scripture of their speech.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those with square heads, it is necessary that the incision of the neck, which is called "epiglottis," be avoided; and this cannot be helped because all the wounds and the pain of the patient are at those who have been struck dumb in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the eyes.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the throat, it is necessary to cut off the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	1. It is therefore necessary, when we wish to cut the epigastrium, that we cut it in three or four circles or one small cut through, between the two circles or according to the quantity of the cut through without damaging the cartilage; and then it is possible to cut the section of the epigastrium without causing any damage, and the vessels are long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	1. And if the masters are too harsh, then it may happen that the neck skin extends to the entire jaw, and then cut the flap as much as it comes to the chin; and avoid the veins of the face, if you see nothing, and then remove the flesh, as we have said; and is demonstrated by the section of the swollen jaw that it should be due to the broken bone of the jaw and due to the lack of voice; and leave the wound overtopped with a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the hour has passed since the injury, gather the two lips of the wound as much as they can, and touch all around the cartilage; then administer medicines that make the wound healthy, as soon as it is clean.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim does not know how to do this until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient is judged to be dying, and the lack of hair.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And since the patient cannot breathe through the epigastrium because of the swelling, and he breathes through the wound, and it is kept alive; and for this reason the ancients commanded to leave the wound over until the malice of the disease is passed, and it has passed in three days or four; and therefore they commanded to suture the wound and cure, as soon as it was cured; and I will tell you what I see.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I see that a maiden is in distress, and she bites her lip, and part of her clothing is torn; and I was called to cure her, and I found her already dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discover the wound, and I find the blood that issued from it, and it was well that she had no veins leading to her neck only, and the blood flowed through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried to the wound and cured it as soon as she became healthy; and she did not remain with the maiden until she was silent, and returned later to her place; therefore I say that there is no cause for pain in the tailoring of the epigastrium.
de la grosse gorge	Of the large mouth
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Hernias are called "hernia of the girdle," and are often large hernias in a red color like a rash, and are more common in women; and there are two types: natural and accidental; where natural has no engine.

dou chancre	The first sentence to translate is "dou
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division of the appearances of chancre, and it is noted that one must overcome by medicines, and it is noted that one must use the cure of iron; and we say that chancre is enjanred in the marris, and great caution in its cure, and we tell the old one that when chancres are in the leu or can be rased if as chancre which is in the mameles, and in the cuixe, and in semblances they are all to be done when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and ancient, if not able to approach it, because I have never seen any healing; nor has anyone ever been healed before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operation, when it is in the flesh or can be opened, is that you never cleanse the patient with black charcoal; then make it cleaner if there is manifest fullness, then cut the flesh at the lower part of the wound to make the operation; then your bones or joints become soft, and all the hair falls out, and the nails of all fall off, and leave the sinew completely loose; let the blood flow freely, and squeeze hard with your hand or on anything, and if the dislocation occurs away from the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize as much as the unclean parts are not affected; then another cure as soon as it is healthy.
de ydropisie	The first sentence to translate is "Ou cautere de
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	The first sentence to translate is "Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And so, the second part.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And so, the second part. The following steps should be taken: If the wound is at the lower belly, and it does not bleed until it reaches the intestine when examined, and cannot be cleaned; then look to see if the fistula is directed towards the intestines: if it comes that you cut it off from the anus III, it must be done directly above the poignil; and if the fistula is due to liver disease, then it should be cut off at the left side of the anus III; and if it is due to the mucus, then it should be cut off at the right, and the patient's pain must not be greater than the pain caused by the superfluities reaching the weak part of the belly; then perforate all the skin with the instrument, and the bougie, and gently press your hand on all the space between the skin and the sycamore as you would when scrunching up a piece of paper or a small piece of cloth; then perforate the sycamore until the space reaches the belly four times, and that is the end of the abscess, then pull out the instrument, and I bougie is in this form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a silver chain, and is of iron or light gold, and in its part it has a small piercing; and sometimes it has three, and sometimes two on one side, and one on another; and the head is cut so that it resembles a quill, and it is the shape of the incision that the scribes make with the quill.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the head of the chief, if it is cut, and when it is sharp, and now you see more than it should be in that hour, by chance if the scribe's spirit is resolved in the arm, or if he has weak hands, or if he is approaching death; but according to the quantity of his valor, and according to what the dispositions of his valor mean, and his wounds; then withdraw the instrument and hold the axe, and it is held now by the heat that stops the piercing that was made at the point which I have spoken of, so that you can do it in this way; then resume the instrument the next day, if you see the scribe suffering from this, and take a small quantity of axe; do this every day, and keep away from it as long as it does not last but a little axe.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	1. And if you doubt the patient, and let them rest for a while, if the care of the tomb or sand bath helps, and by washing or bathing and in the sun, and becomes flushed; and the care of drying medicines as soon as they are healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and liver and spleen after the removal of the fever, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	2. of the prevention of the winter
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	3. No child is ever born without having a cough in the winter, or if the cough is small, or it is not heavy in his chest.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is not perceived at all, even with great care, according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then place the cloth underneath, and tie it with the string, and leave it for three to four hours or eight, and if you see urine, then collect it and make urine, and then put it back; and by chance, they may not fit, because the urine that comes out will not close.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the cloth used is too small, then it should be treated with a piece of cloth, as we have said, if it stretches.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the cloth in their loins are cold because no one is born with the cloth at the top of the thigh, for they cannot urinate before they do not cut off their thigh; and they cannot enlarge because of this, as the material cannot come close enough to the marrow, and it is a serious disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	The manner of the wound if the patient gushes blood from his back, is that it is the head of the vein and the copula as big as a penny, if it pierces the flesh, if it comes; and you must prevent the loss of blood that comes often, and if it comes, if the wound is clean, and cure the wound as much as it is healthy.
des pustules de la verge	of the vein's pustules
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times, pustules come in the vein, and it looks like a bad appearance; and some are malignant and not malignant; if you must clean them under the subcutaneous fat, and cut and mound all, then put on cotton fluff in Egyptian ointment; then the care of ointment is done as much as it is healthy.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	If the tumor is malignant, of a dark color and fast-growing, then you must have the cauterization.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	After you have cauterized it, and the tumor is still present, and it has parts that are dense and parts that are sparse, then you must remove the part that was dense; and if it remains, then treat the sparse part.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you remove it all together, if you do not ensure that the head of the tumor is not felt, and it becomes black and corrupt in its head and in the surrounding area; then remove all that is black and corrupt, then apply honey and flour made from the scabs of green pumpkins and vines, then other cures as long as it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if the dislocation occurs, then follow this method of lunar cauterization according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if the cauterization helps in the following two positions: it is knowledge that the dislocation occurred and the corruption; and if the head of the thorn is corrupted and retracts, then you should either bind or lead the thorn with a string of wire, and let the mucus flow from it; and when the pelz (thorn) comes to the end of the verge (thorn) that has not been circumcised, or has been caused by a wound or abscess, then you should scrape it with the instrument cheveit (razor), as long as the liiens (ligatures) are loosened, and release the chief of the verge from all parts; and if this is difficult to do, then scrape the thorn of the verge and the peil (hair) without any element between them, and then wet the subtle drapeil of lin moilliet an aigue froide (cold linen cloth), so it does not cause pain.
de la circoncision	The first sentence to translate is "Ou cautere de
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a continuous disfigurement like other wounds; however, if we perform this work out of our own will and for the benefit of our children, and in fact it is the best work and the most gentle for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not often circumcise their children, for they did not use it in their law, and have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I want the greatest part of masters and physicians who performed circumcision in the old way, with force, and at all ages; if it were not for the fact that it causes pain, and by chance if one could not find another, and had to do it oneself.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or they recover quickly, and the pain is double, and at circumcision which is hard for the point of the member; and at the circumcision of the finger by chance it breaks the iron, and causes the wound to open, and many times are born prematurely, and I want none of that.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	The first line of the text translates to: "Of the mondification that is made with forces, I have found the benefit of the experiment, because the forces cut just as well on the top as on the bottom.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The second line of the text translates to: "For when you press your hand, if it cuts evenly in one direction, but that the thread is not too thick on the other side; and that the manner of the first stitch is such that it seems to the child that you only tie the thread around the verge, and then I do so in all ways you please; then I do it right between my hands, and put the forces between my hands or between my fingers that the children do not see, nor any of the instruments; then pin your hand to the verge and blow or sneeze, and lift it up as much as the head of the verge is assembled, then mend well the dirt that is on it, then tie the lew sign intended for a double thread, then tie it to the other lien; and keep it as you do in the second reading in the pouch and the index, and cover between the two threads, then gently pull down the curtain and draw the chief of the verge; then leave the sanc poc and poc, for they are the worst; and put powder on and on powder I put the powder of a dried bacon cooked without spice, preserved with rose oil and fresh, and let it rest for another day, and cure it further as long as it is healthy.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces at the incision is as follows: the two ends should be even and smooth, and should be as large as the corresponding part.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the incision is when the edges come out at the incision; therefore, it should be extended to your nail, and if it does not fit well, then it should be held in place with your nail, and then it will hold.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they remain for three days, and the wound is infected, then it should be left to heal as long as the sore does not become inflamed, and it should be lightly scorched; if the wound is as you hold it, and you protect it from the part of the wound, it will not hurt you.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	The patient's leg wound should be treated with poultices made from sourdough powder, as we have mentioned or used in the past, and if it does not improve, it will go worse; treat the wound as we have said, as soon as it is healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	Retainment of urine.
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	Retention of urine due to dysuria, cystitis, bowel obstruction, intestinal blockage, or similar conditions, as we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine is discharged, and you see the retention by the urethra which is at the anus or columella of the vagina, then it should be noted that the patient's hips are caught on his own thighs; and he should have his legs extended from the back, and his abdomen is expanded from the part below the back, and restricted his hips to the expression of the urethra at the desire of the urine, as soon as it comes, if it does not come, and the patient feels great pain, then it should be noted that you should administer an extraction with all the instruments called "siringue", and its form is: and it should be made of fine silver hair, like the feather of a sparrow; and it should be the tail of a palm leaf about half a meter long, and it should be made fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	Here is the translation of the first line: "And the manner of the urine's exit if you take a double thread, and tie it at the tip of the wool or linen, and cut the tip of the thread with the sewing needle; and cut off the excess of the wool and cut the tip of the thread, then anoint the thread with oil or balsam and olive oil and vinegar of garden, and make the patient sit on the seat, and the bladder and the urethra are moistened with oil and olive oil and vinegar of garden; then gently insert the thread into the urethra, as far as it reaches to the root of the urethra, then double the urethra towards the bulb; then cut the thread before the bladder, and feel the patient come out the empty bladder, and this is done according to this order because either the conductor or the patient is tense; then the thread is all through the hair, and the urine follows the hair, then it is drawn out, and the urine is made up; and the siringue resumes when the bladder is empty and the patient's urethra is healed.
des maladies de la vessie	Of illnesses of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there is scorbutus or blood in the bladder, or when there is pus assembled, and you see water and medicines distilling, then do this to all the instrument called "clepsadra", and it is shaped like:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if there are three pulses: two on one side and one on the other, as you see; and it is read by the medicine that is so hot that it burns well the verge with addition, if one can draw the moisture, and let it be; and when you see your medicines gushing in the bladder, put the head of the clister in the moisture, and draw it with the drawing which is ens; if you draw the moisture with the clister, and then forcefully draw the traction which is ens; if the moisture enters, and comes to the bladder now, if that the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle clyster that one clisters the bladder: if that is:

Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I said that emorroydes and thrombosis, when they are formed in the arm, do not appear by touching, if it is not by the care of a surgeon.

Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	1. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then remove the nails from the horseshoe, and cut off the roots of the horse, then powder some medicines restricting blood, such as ice and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then pour water on her feet for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if she loses blood, it comes out if you make a decoction of sumac and the root of grapefruit, apples, and pears, and similar things, and then take flour of barley, mix it with honey and hazelnut, and apply it on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	If it is dislocated, it is bad.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If it is not dislocated, make the patient lie on their back and massage gently to avoid hurting; then take the joint, and the milk in the juice of plantain or aloe with wine vinegar, and massage the joint.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the wound is healed, if you dress the leg with ointment until it is healthy; and the one called "albathir" is red and resembles the sharp end of a thorn, if it corresponds to my saying the thistle, then you dress it as I said until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	Of the plaices of the arm
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	There are many types of wounds that come to the arm in the marris, such as chancres and abscesses, herpes, gashes, fistulas, and blisters, and other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, it is necessary that I treat the gash wound that comes to the arm in this chapter, which is not different from other wounds that bow; and if you see the evil of fire, look at whether the wound is already at its beginning when it comes, and signs of chill and fever, and if it becomes red, you will see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	For this reason, do not hasten to percuss, but make him endure as long as the pain is assuaged; then place the patient on his side, and have him lie on two pillows until his thigh is straight; let his knees be widely apart, and support his back and assemble his heels at the end of the thigh; let his fingers be expanded, and put his hands on his knees, and tie them well with a belt; then move the instrument towards the left side, and after that comes the form; it is necessary that when you see him handling this instrument, you fix the first part to know the fitting of the marriage bed, so that what enters through the instrument does not fit more than it should, and does not distort the patient's hand; and if it is larger, it is necessary to cover the fitting of the marriage bed with cloths, so that the patient is not grieved; and it is necessary that he places the handle of the instrument at the end, and draws the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	1. And when the abscess is opened and it is touched with a clean hand, if it covers the head, apply oil to the wound; and when the bowel is seen, if it comes that you must put tents in the wound softened in olive oil or olive oil, and put the tent for the wound at the end of the mare, and put it on the mare and on the cut nail smoothly washed with cold or warm ointment; then the cure after two days of dressing, as long as it is healthy; and never lift the mare and the wound by a cloth of cold or honey, and then of cold or roots of licorice and aristotle are cooked; then repeat the dressing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is closed in the marriage, then you must not cook with iron, but cure as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbearing
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Mastery is first in the dance that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs if you see the woman press against the wall, and desire to smell the aroma: therefore, help the children to be born; then you should know that these children are according to the natural figure, and they are from his own offspring, and the second one with him; and when you see these signs, it is appropriate to gently press on his belly so that the child is soon; for when he descends from his head, if it is with his second one, and is monied by good cleanliness, then this marriage comes otherwise naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier. Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child is born naturally, and the woman gives birth with great pain, and her virtues are weak, if it is placed on a stool or in women's hands, and she is cooked with olive oil or fenugreek, then the dance begins between its two little spatula, which is its form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes. Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the hands come out further, then it is necessary to lightly reset them a little at a time; and if they do not enter, then the woman should sit on the bed, and lift the feet up; then pull the bed down on the ground, and tie it to the woman so that it does not fall; and if the hands cannot be set, and the child dies, then cut the hands at the point that is before us, and take the child out, and reset it as evenly as possible.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	Of the issue of the child with its feet

de plusors enfans	The phrase "de plusors enfans" translates to

De plusors enfans" translates to "No children are formed in the marris I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more than XV, and they are all formed as a child by the measurement of the old glorious wife, and cover the whole body because of chance, as it seems; if you follow this, then.
de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child

Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly some children had died, then consulted another about this, and he said that death was the cause.

Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est. dou fremit	The first sentence to translate is "dou
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Antor is a small appearance that should appear in the chest, and it moves with every breath; and no time does the fever disappear, and it feels like death's trembling, and it comes throughout the body, and more than the hands than any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the remedy is that if you take a thorn from a goose feather, or a very sharp vulture's feather, and put it on the trembling, as long as the purple circle encircles the trembling all around; then turn your hand over all the thorn so that you cover all around the trembling, and put it in place, and cut off the roots of the trembling.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	If you see, if I make a needle of iron or steel according to this form, and it is subtle and thin:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	If you see, if the cauterization moves, if it is in front of or in the chapter of cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clyster.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No time has it been made of silver or archae, or of melted iron or hammered; and no time has it been made of these small and large bowels, according to which they are distributed.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, these are made in the treatment of children and weak and painful ones, they are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and great clister is such that when it is large, the belly is lined in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is a deviation or the belly is lined in this manner: the head of the clister is visible, and the shoulder is dislocated perceived; and it is at one of the costals, and at the other; and it is the belly or where medicines are placed in a vessel of a beast or parchment, and all the holes of the small pertus are perceived, and between each pertus there must be a spice, then weave through each pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort in X or more entor, and assemble the belly as if it were a swine; and when the medicine is given, if the line is at the instrument before with a strong thread, then clisterize; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	1. And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head with oil or unguent of urine or similar thing, then gently apply it; then the surgeon takes his two hands and assembles them as much as possible, until it is all done, then he removes the clyster, and gently supports the patient's legs at the pillow, and if the medicine comes out, as much as it can; and if the patient sleeps a whole night, it will be more helpful.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	2. And if you clysterize the patient with a disease of diarrhea of the stomach, and the medicine comes out, if it recurs as soon as it is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the swelling is either from the foundation or the gangrene, whether it is the clyster also subtle as in a child; and this is the form of the subtle clyster that is drawn when the skin is stretched.
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said the cure of wounds in the division; and you will say the cures of hands and medicine, according to the completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the tools or weapons used, and how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the point of the weapon, and the size of the spearhead or lance, or dart, or javelin, or other things; or they are made according to the tools of the hands, as if a wound is made at the neck, or at the shoulder, or elbow, or side, or belly, or liver, and other members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds on the shoulder, because the reminder will be in his chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or head, and the bone is not broken, if it is due to bleeding or similar things, and the skin is completely torn off and the wound is large, and you slightly doubt of hemorrhage: if the head itself becomes healthier than the affected part; and avoid the physician's surfeit of wine and fatty foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not become healthier, if the meat is anemic, and does not drink wine, and does not eat char, and puts the wound on fire, and comes with a thin ointment, either of oil or vinegar only; and if it does not come with a post, when the wound is fresh and not moved by the air, dust, which I will say a little later; and if the wound is moved, then puts on some gargles, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	When the wound is large, like that of a spearhead and its surroundings, and the lips cannot be reassembled by tents, if they can be reassembled by stitching, just as I will say about belly wounds, by sewing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is discovered to be bone, it can be pulled out, and it holds only by a point, if the nail; then treat the wound with medicine, restore hardness in the leather of the shoe, and order the patient to eat large meats, such as testes and cooked flour, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	When you touch the skin, and it does not reach the bone, and it causes pain, then the cure is to apply a poultice of herbs. And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by medicine, if you need to stop the artery, and you loosen it with a thread; and if this does not help, if it is cauterized.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the lightest cure is sufficient: and that you apply this poultice that has the smell of herbs.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the way of the poultice is: take a part of incense; mix with three parts of dragon's blood; and three parts of live chalz, and the fine powder, and apply to the wound, and draw it together as much as it can and stick to all its edges; and then close it well, and leave it to dry, so that it does not ooze if it swells; because the medicine is not used until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never has it been done with any tool alone, when there is no incense or sacrifice to the dragon, but that the art has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the art has moved the wound, at once in this way; but do not use my powder; rather use some digested ointments or flour made from barley and honey, as it bows down; then continue with other cures until it is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then use fine tweezers to remove it; and I will tell you more about this later in the chapter on major fractures.
de la plaie dou col	Of the wound of the shoulder
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	A wound comes from the shoulder
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the shoulder, and there is no other cause but to treat the wound, and do not restrict anything, as it will retract itself; and do not put anything on the wound, as the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of this with the brain is the more sensitive members; but if the medicine is cold, like lavender in gentle water, and mixed with rose oil, and lavender washed in gentle water, and other pierces of this kind, and moistened ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is large, and it is bound with bandages, then the care is as long as it takes for it to heal.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If the wounds are deep and long, and they are full of blood, and if the vein is pierced, and the artery is cut, and the blood comes out, and it is stopped, and the wound is cauterized, and the spine of the neck is cut, or the teeth, and the mouth is guarded, as long as the tooth is in the jaw of the neck, and it is not touched but replaced according to its natural figure; then the extraction is performed, and a few days are left, then the care for dressings is done as soon as it heals; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, if it wants; and if there are pieces of bone, if they are not too large, and those that cannot be, leave them as long as the wound is sore, and it is dressed and becomes healthy and sound; and if the wound is fresh, and powder is applied as I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	If there is an abscess in the wound and it has been incised, as I have described in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of the arrow or the spear.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If the wound is of an arrow or spear, and it is gushing blood, then look at the wound and see if there is any signs of death: if so, then the wound is mortal; and if it is not gushing blood, and it is fresh all around the wound, then do not delay in applying the powder at the first hour, nor bind it with the wound, but keep it on the chest, and observe the patient; but if you have no ointment, then put cotton in the wound to dry out the moisture, and make the patient sleep over the wound for three or four hours, or more, until the spasm or trembling of the chest does not cause any discomfort; and when you see the bones in good order, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the wounds and other treatments as necessary to make them healthy; and if it cannot be made healthy, cleanse and dress it with what has been used before; as is necessary.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	If the wound is a cut or puncture with simple blood flow, and it is in front or on the back, if the treatment is by the one who is in front; if it is large, use poultice; and if it is small, use powder, and if it is in the bone, and if it pierces pieces, if the wound wants to be exposed, and if they are not exposed, let it be exposed if the extractions are removed; and for other wounds of other members, judge as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	The first sentence to translate is "dou derrompement dou ventre". The translation of
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The first sentence to translate is "dou derrompement dou ventre". The translation of "dou derrompement dou ventre" is "great and severe abdominal pain, no intestine ever being torn once, or the intestines being torn, and the wound is more painful, and never a small wound is as painful as a large one, because the intestines are repeatedly inserted; because the intestines swell so much that they feel the sting, if they are inserted more often, and because it causes more pain, because the intestine is frequently torn, because the intestine is frequently reinserted at its place where others have been. And there are four ways in which the abdominal pain is caused: the two common wounds come in the abdominal wound, and the other wounds of the belly and chest are also common, and all of them are more severe with the abdominal wound, and I will say one each and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and there is no inflammation in the intestines, and it is difficult to set, this is one of the two ways: either because of the size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is twisted due to the blow.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is twisted, you should treat it in this way: soften a sponge or a damp cloth only, or wet it with hot water, add vinegar and salt, and gently pull on the intestine until it unwinds; never force it, and it will come out easily.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	When you see the inflammation departing, if the intestine of the anus or anus and rectum are cooked, it is because this is the cause of the entrance of a little thing; and if it cannot enter, then make a small wound with the instrument on the cut, and cover the blood with the dressing; and the first cure is to cut off that part, which is not necessary to cut off in great necessity, and this is the stranger for the fence: if it cuts through the neck and does not close, and sees its form.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine jumps, if it is reset according to its natural form in its own place, you will be well off, because this is good.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is wide, and it is in the lower abdominal region, if you want to make the patient lie down on his back, and raise his legs higher than his chest; and if it is in the lower abdominal region, then he should raise his head and legs higher than the parts below, and thus he will strain his abdomen in one of the two parts as agreed upon, depending on which part is higher; and it is necessary to administer what I say in large and gaping wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	When the wound is small, and it is in the lower abdominal region, if you want to make the patient lie down on his back, and raise his legs higher than his chest; and if it is in the lower abdominal region, then he should raise his head and legs higher than the parts below, and thus he will strain his abdomen in one of the two parts as agreed upon, depending on which part is higher; and it is necessary to administer what I say in large and gaping wounds. If the wound is small, then it is necessary to sew it with a needle, and assemble the lips; and this is the common way of sutures, and it is that you prick one or more needles, according to the size of the wound, then leave the end of the wound free, and pass one or two threads through the end of the wound, as you sew the wound from that side; then assemble the ends of the thread with the ends of the suture, which is the skin of the wound, as far as you can sew the part, and assemble the ends of the suture in four places; then pull the thread tight around the needle, then assemble the ends of the wound with the ends of the suture, and leave the end of the suture free, and pass another needle through it, as you have done with the first needle, and continue doing so according to the needles you have, until all the wound is closed; the needles should be fine, between subtle and thick, because the fine needles penetrate the whole skin, and the thick ones do not enter well; therefore they should be fine; and it is not necessary to insert the needles too close to the wound and the skin, because they can cause the wound to open before the suture is dry; then sew the ends of the needles, so that the patient does not bleed while sleeping, and put covers or blankets on the ends of the needles, so that they are held in place as long as the wound is sore; then pull the thread tight around the needle, then assemble the ends of the wound with the ends of the suture, and leave the end of the suture free, and pass another needle through it, as you have done with the first needle, and continue doing so according to the needles you have, until all the wound is closed; the needles should be fine, between subtle and thick, because the fine needles penetrate the whole skin, and the thick ones do not enter well; therefore they should be fine; and it is not necessary to insert the needles too close to the wound and the skin, because they can cause the wound to open before the suture is dry;
