Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I relieved the intestine, and it had been twenty-four hours since it was injured, and the wound was fifty years old, and the doctor treated it, and it became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the nurse measured the pulse to see if it would stop, and it was a miracle; and I did not use any medicine, as there were none in the league where no one was found, nor any medicines; and I washed the wound with vinegar twice a day, and the cotton swab with honey as much as it became healthy.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or you will tell me the two most common ways of sewing: take the needle, and pull it through the corner of the fabric; when it has perceived the right direction in the right direction, if the point or side or where you pulled the needle is not straight, and make it pass through another part of the uneven part; and the stitches are understood if you do as the tailor does with the fur, and leave once the seam one way, and take it back again, until the stitch is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	1. The second method of sewing, which Galen called his own, is done in this way: if anyone does it correctly, they bring together the two ends naturally and apply one of the corners of the thread to the other, like this: make a needle or corner of iron approach close, and only the two threads of iron; then turn the needle, and make it perpendicular to the part that is most dense, as the two threads of iron; then make it perpendicular to the part that is most dense on both sides of the thread, using other corners of iron that are on the other side; and this is the better way of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	1. If the patient hears this speech and no one testifies, then it is necessary to sew the abdomen around the needles, or they should be tied in each; and it must be one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those that are twisted corroded; and it is feared that when the rupture is near the abdomen, it is more painful than other bellies.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	1. The judgment of the wound is whether it is like the judgment of other wounds: and if you truly touch the fresh wound with all its sutures, unless it has moved, then reinsert the intestine and the bowel; then put on the powdered charcoal, and if it has moved, then apply any ointment that is present, as long as the wound is bowed; and cut the thread, and be sure the stitch is tight, and the knot is secure; then cure the wound as you would with other wounds, as long as it is healthy; and if you have no medicines, then put them on, as much as they come out of the bowels, a cloth full of vinegar, and rub it twice in the morning until it is healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have no other skill in other positions than wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not become infected as the principal members, then it comes that you lightly apply oil of temperate chalor, or oil of rose, and put on the bandages, and loose the garter; and if there is pain or soreness in the belly, and many times it comes, if the clitoris is cleaned with red wine, and at the same time the soreness comes to the intestine; and the perches are pierced, and sauced that when it is the large intestines, it is lighter to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The small intestine that is called "young" cannot heal until it is cut, and this is due to the fragility of its walls and the subtlety of the entire body, as well as its proximity to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe. de la routure dou boueil	Of the bursting of the bowels
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine bursts, and the wound is small, if it can be restored with a few stitches, because I have seen that some were healed or wounded by a lance; and this was the wound on the left side of the stomach, and it became a fistula and the egestion and vomiting passed through it; I treated it according to what I could, and did not stop subtly until it was healed, and I examined it.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it healed, I doubted that the patient had no harm in his belly; but he had none, but delayed in better preparations, and drank and ate; and they said to no one whoever had a small wound in the intestine, that one must clean it in this way: first make large knots, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the mouth has overstretched it, put it between the lips, if it pulls the mouth between them; and then tie the knot, and hold it so that it cannot slip, and then make another twist in the same way as before, until the wound is completely closed; and then close the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	1. If the end of the intestine is inflamed and causes no harm to the patient, and it can be tied with a thread as fine as a hair from a beast, in this way: take the end of this thread from the intestine that is loose, and then tie it to the end of this fil line of silk, then cut the thread with the needle, and sew through the intestine, and then knot the intestine; and this manner of stitching is not harder than according to the course of love and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, even when it is in one of the large intestines, if it does not become gangrenous or infected, it will be enough if it is subtle.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Of a fistula or if it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	That all wounds and abscesses, when they heal, are called fistulas, and also when they are thin and have a small opening.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the belief that it must be hard and wheal-like, and one feels pain, and is as thin as the tail of an ostrich; and never with a clear opening, and sometimes wide; never small, and sometimes large; never shallow, and sometimes deep; and I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that all wounds that are not healed and do not hurt, it is only because of one of the seven causes: it is to know, because of the small amount of pus or blood; or because of its malice; or because it has too many bowels, which does not allow the wound to heal; or the lesion is porous, and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is like a pestilence; or because of the property in the region is delayed digestion, and delayed health, and runs through nature; or it has voines or os: and I have shown all these causes and their signs and cures with medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	The correct translation of the given line is: "And it is necessary for me to inform you about the treatment of fistulas, which is made by human hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	The correct translation of the given line is: "Fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from great veins, arteries, nerves, or the subcutaneous tissue, or the intestine, or the bladder, or any of the ribs, or the spine, or any joint of the hands or feet; and if it comes to affect a part of the body's original member, and resembles these.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	The correct translation of the given line is: "And all these fistulas of this kind are of bad omen, and only labor and ignorance; and if there is no fistula that does not come from the part I have mentioned, and you are seeking the cure, and you see it applied, then take a nail or a piece of iron, if the fistula is straight, as you wish; and if the fistula is bent, then search for it with a very fine needle, for the points are bent in the bending; and if the fistula is in the hands and you do not find it well by needles, then take a piece of the pertus where it is, as it is more cort than any other part of the pertus, and makes it whole; then you will know if it is bone or nerve, and whether it is smooth or rough, and ask the patient to tell you about the pain he feels when you press his hand with yours, and the leu or where it is, and whether it is far from the joint, or the nerve, or the artery or vein, or any of the parts I have mentioned, if the coping is according to what I have said, and then the cure will be safe and the charred parts that are corrupted will be removed; and then the cure, when it is sound, and the fistula is well made in its right place, if you cop with your hand as you press, then take fine needles in medicine ague, and insert them at the end of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that has been added to the fount; and then take clean ointments in a healthy jar, as it should be; and if it is not healthy, then the cauterization is done as we have said, and if the os is corrupted by the fistula, then the coping is done as we have said.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If you have pain in the bones or limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is discovered, and it becomes corrupt and black, as long as the corruption remains, treat the dislocated parts as if they are healthy; and when they become healthy, return to normal; and if they are not healthy, then be aware that you will have to do this: if you dislocate the bone and want to put it back in place as soon as possible, and remove all the corruption, then restore the bone; and if it becomes healthy, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os. Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	1. If you do not open the wound within an hour, put something on the wound that is slightly moistening, and leave it until the pus has run out of the bones; then if the bones are lighter, and it is only a large bone such as a thigh or knee, if you only let the corruption run so that the blackness is all gone, then restore the wound; and if a large part of the bone is corrupted and comes out of the bone, if it can be sewn and covered with something to stop the corruption, and then treated as much as possible, and I will tell you about a fistula that came out in your leg, so that you can take it as an example and help in your practice.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	The young man was thirty years old, who had a pain in his leg from an cause that came from the chest, so much that the materials came to the leg, and he fell into a large abscess, and there was no reason to open; but the women overpowered it so much that the abscess burst, and corroded with matters, and became a fistula, and many wounds of belly and cold chest came out; and they treated him for two years, and there was no knowledge in the art of hands, as soon as I was called, and saw his leg and the medicines used on it, and what corroded from the wounds of the cold chest; and his chest became red with his youth, and had a yellowish color.

I thought thus, and pushed into the hole as far as I could see a part of the bone, and found it rotten and perished, and the corruption was right up to the bone's end; I knew that what I saw was rotten bone, and I wanted to make sure there was no more corruption, so I began to restore the wound with ointments for a long time, but I could not suture; then I opened it again, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and I treated it, and then I closed the wound, but I could not glue the flesh because it was all rotten, so I restored it with ointments; it became healthy and healed quickly, and I did not want to repeat the operation for the fear of the patient's suffering, which he could not endure, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For because of the frequent evacuation of blood, but it was completely healthy, and a hard char was found on the bone, and it was in good position and had no harm or contrary effect at all, neither in the limb nor in coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in no part of the limb, then it should be set in this way: take the wires, and draw them at the head of the bone which is open, and command that they do not extend above; and put another wire of larger diameter than the first, and lay it on the char that is out of the bone, and tie it at the head, so that you can draw the corrupted char away from the limb, and cut the char off where you see it set, that it may not crush the char; and put a bandage or a table on the bone to cover the corrupted char; and set as many times as you can see and feel the corruption, and set again another time.

The cure of iron is done in two ways: one is on the part where it is painful, and you take out the dark blood; and the other way is that you tie the vein, and pull it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The first sentence to translate is: "The size of the wound is according to this manner: first, cut the hot leg with a sharp knife until it is not subtle, then tighten the leg with the help of the hands of the masseur, pressing on the part below the knee; then cut the vein in one, two, or three places, of a large size, then ease and tie off the black blood with your hand, from one to the other, as much as you can without causing too much pain to the patient's strength; then close it, and command that it be sewn with black threads; and continue the evacuation and cleaning of the wounds as the veins become smooth, and leave it to the masseur.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. When the leg of the patient is cold, if it has hair, then wash it with warm water, and dry the leg with a cloth until it turns red, and heat the foot; and if there is no fire, then heat the foot with fire, and then place it on the cold part of the knee or below the ankle; then apply leather to the toe, and burn the leg from all sides, until it turns red and black, and when it becomes black and white, as if it were a blunted thread; then cut the leather off, as soon as it is dry, and then place it on the other thigh, and three times; then burn the leather along the leg until it turns red, and then smooth it with the heel, as you have done, and place it on another thigh, if you have more, and then smooth it, and place it at the second point; then take it out of the tailor's tailor, as soon as it is all done, and the tailor; and if you do not take it out of the tailor's tailor, and raise it, if it bites a double thread, and cut it and pull it, and cut the tailor's tailor, and turn your hand in both directions, until it is; and keep it from being cut, for if it is cut, if you cannot touch or lift it, and it comes near to the patient; and when you have treated it, put a poultice of fine linen moistened with wine and rose oil on the wound; and cure it as soon as it is healthy.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	When the vis (or limb) is contracted, twisted, and enveloped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, if you must cut it painfully, but do not cut it completely; and the traction (or pulling) is as we have mentioned before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of iron that is used to cut the limb if it is twisted, and does not cut too deeply, so as not to cut the vein; and it is a thick gouge, because if it were too fine, it would cut the vein, but if it is thick, as we have said, and this is the form:
de la voinne civile	of the vein of the arm.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is infected in the legs, in hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth where there is no moisture; and by chance it may occur in other parts than in the legs, and this is caused by flesh that comes out of the hide, just as it does from the tail of a snake and turns, infecting between the hide and the char.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there is a very great inflammation in the leg, then it changes its color, and begins to bleed, just as a root of a plant does.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	If the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation. The shoulder is infected in the legs, in hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth where there is no moisture; and by chance it may occur in other parts than in the legs, and this is caused by flesh that comes out of the hide, just as it does from the tail of a snake and turns, infecting between the hide and the char. If the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there is a very great inflammation in the leg, then it changes its color, and begins to bleed, just as a root of a plant does. If the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation. And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there is a very great inflammation in the leg, then it changes its color, and begins to bleed, just as a root of a plant does. If the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	1. And no time at this vein hands rain, and moreover when it opens in the joint of either shoulder or both, and then comes out with pustules, and which jumps rain; cure the latter as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	2. Those that are born between leather and horn.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	3. This disease is called in our land "disease of beef," because it often occurs in cattle, and is a small worm that goes up and down between leather and horn, and passes through all the limbs from head to toe, and causes great pain in the limbs as it goes up and down, and sometimes it goes to the belly; and it is caused by the humors of some animals, such as serpents, snakes, and ascarides or worms in the belly; and one doubts its malice, because when it goes through the limbs, it goes up to the head, and sometimes it returns, and destroys the brain. And this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see the wound healing and drying, if it can only be that when he will: if it comes to pass that you examine the leg and find it well-closed, then close it and cut it off, and put it in a vessel of hot water, and do not touch it if it is cauterized with fire as long as it lives; and the greatest harm it can do, if it is that it touches oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or going near the oil, if the corners of the mouth are formed, then close it, and cut it off; and it is necessary to use the cauterant with disinfection of solutions of medicines for the humors of the body, and avoid eating spicy foods as nourishment.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from the pain that comes from wind
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "winding" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in certain parts of the body, and spreads from one part to another; and I see what I have told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called a female patient, and I saw my arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of my shoulder; and later, I saw it rise as quickly as any thing, as if it were living silver when it cut through the flesh of my shoulder; the pain left that part, and spread to the shoulder, and then a little while later spread throughout the body, until it came to the other shoulder; then she told me that it turned inside out across the body, as I see.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I am surprised to see how it moves from limb to limb, as I have never wanted this disease to happen in this way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Indeed, I wanted to make sure that the pain was not transferred from one limb to another, but I did not want it, as I see it in the woman; and I thought it was because the woman had dry breasts, and the veins were exposed, and because this constraint appeared; and I did not know if it was for this reason in those who are delicate, and who have dry breasts and veins replenished.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	When you see the patient being cured of this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said, if the limb is not quickly reduced, and then hold it until the constraint is released at the joint; and cauterize the joint; and if you do not see this with your own eyes, if the cure of this which relieves the constraint, if like pills of sinew, and pills of hemp, and similar things.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows come in various types, according to their appearances and according to the wounds they cause in the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of arrows is such that some have long points, and short, and sharp, and blunt; and some have angles, and some have curves, and some have pieces; and one that pierces any member in different ways: either in the principle members like hair, skin, liver, spleen, lungs, intestines, uterus, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When the pain becomes unbearable in any of these limbs, and the sign of death appears, which I will tell you later, you perceive: if you intend to remove this arrow, for death follows in its wake; and when this sign does not appear, and the wound is not deep, then cut it out and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of great pain appears when the arrow pierces the bone and causes the eye to jump, which is the one that was suspended by the eye socket, and it is characterized by scotomie and sode and esvertin and roujor of the limbs, and inflammation and roujor of the tongue, and spasme and permixtion of understanding, and vomiting of cole; and by chance it is not caused by the nose or ears; and by chance it affects the speech and voice; and a sudden jump of the white wound-like pus resembling poppets, and in that jump as well as a cough like that of a horse; and if this sign appears, if you hold on to the treatment, and remove the arrow if it is not deep.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the shoulder when it is pressed or cut is that it hurts or feels hard as if it were stuck in something solid; and by chance the shoulder becomes motionless like the leg, and in a short time black blood comes out, and there is cold sweat and cold frost, and the patient feels doubt that the death is near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the eye that is not opening is that there are no signs of swelling from the wound, and the gum is inflamed, and the face turns pale, and he sighs high and cries out in pain.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the eye is pressed in the covering of the head, it hurts the small ribs; and there is great pain and sighing and trembling; and all the members of the shoulder are moved.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow hits the thigh or stomach by chance, then there is no digestion of the meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow hits the thigh or stomach, and there is no hope in the treatment, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow hits the bladder and the urine jumps out and comes out forcefully, and the patient feels great pain: these are fatal wounds.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, if the face, neck, throat, shoulder, and back are affected, and the limb seems, they are saved according to different conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the bone or artery is in the flesh and it is not moving, as I will tell you if I remember, because you are doing it wrong.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to my home a bone that was cut or broken at the root of the ear: I tried to set it, and from another part I removed the grease from the ear, and it became healthy.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I found a bone that was cut or broken in the grease of the oil of the paper of the ear, and the bone was set, and it could not be reached but to the point of the loud fist, and it was as large as a Turkish bow, all of it light for the ears; the joint was healthy, and I never had any accidents.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And there was a gash in the throat of a creature, and it was the Arabian ear: I was the hair, and subtle as I passed, and it was healthy for the creatures.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And there was a gash in my belly, which I thought would kill me; and then if it did not change its position within 30 days, I would cut out the gash, sew it up, and it would heal, and there would be no further accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if your home has a gash in the back or buttocks, and it was caused by a wound; and the gash did not heal, and did not follow its natural dispositions, and did not find any harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see another man, who was pricked by an arrow in his face, and suffered from the wound; and it took a long time to suffer great pain; and of other kinds.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And found an arrow in the shoulder of a prince, the king, who was buried in the neck, and was slightly curved to the right side; and it was completely embedded when I was called for treatment after three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound to be very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I examined it with all my subtlety, and I did not feel anything; but I felt a sharp and painful sensation in the right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought that this was the end of the rib I placed the sharp, dry digestive juice on it, because the rib did not burn; and I saw that it was from the rib.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the salve to my hands, and relieved the right side of the wound, and delayed the patient's pain for a long time, until he felt the rib and his limbs; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied the poisonous salve to the wound with my hands, as it was overgrown, and I peeled it off, and I felt the end of the rib that was attached to the limb; then I applied more of the poisonous salve to the wound through the salve, until the head of the rib appeared visibly; and it healed well in four months, and then I removed the stitches and the nails on both sides, and could not; therefore I continued to refine and invent ways to splint, as soon as I had good stitches made with my nails, according to how the form comes at the end of this chapter, as I mend it and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	The patient suspects that the cartilage in the nose cannot be restored: I will restore it accordingly, and the wound was sore, but the pain in the nose was completely relieved.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you about the quality of extracting some arrows, so you should use your judgment, as the books cannot make everything look perfect; but the masters of the craft can do well with a few good things, and with what is present and deficient, they perform nine operations, and use nine instruments, as the things extracted in this art descend.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come from the limbs or they are false if according to two ways: either by the shoulder or they enter, or by another part; and the one that passes through the eye or it enters, is an arrow that has entered in the eyes, and it will never pass again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	If she does not jump now, if she lets it be as the char is burned all over and the issue comes out; and then she gets stuck in the bone, and she cannot move if she leaves any joints, and each joint; and therefore she jumps, and if she does not jump, if she perceives through the entire body subtly, as long as the char is burned all over and the issue comes out, and then she turns.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the shoulder, and it goes into one of the bellies of the head, or some of the accidents I have told the midwife: if she does not remove it, but lets it be as long as it is even after some joints, because if she removes it it comes out to bleed, it is the death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the dislocation is not evident except in the bone alone, and does not cause any sudden pain, and the patient has no other previous injuries, then it is not a cause for concern.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is not evident and cannot be corrected, then it should be treated as soon as possible, as I have told you; then treat the limb until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the dislocation is not visible in the limb alone, and cannot be seen, and the patient insists on trying to correct it; and if you feel it, and there is no suitable instrument available; and if you do not want to cause further pain or damage to the wound, and the joint is swollen but there are no nerves involved, and the dislocation is not too far, and you treat the limb as much as possible, and if the ears of the limb are held in place, and you break or twist them gently, until you can treat them; and carefully, even if you break the joint, you should treat it more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you do not press once, if the bone is still in place until it is read, then pull, because the extraction is difficult.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If the dislocation moves against the will, if you ignore what we have said in this chapter; and you are warned of the incision on the nerve and vein, and put in the position you want to remove the arrow, either firmly or gently, or closed or elemental; and you put the bandage according to the shape it was when the arrow came out, because it is the greatest help that can be given, and if you do not, if you put it according to what they show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The first line of the text translates to: "The arrowhead that comes from another part, or it opens nothing of his, or the hide is curled in some place where one can see or feel differently: then pull it out, as much as the barbs can hold, and then extract: if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if the arrowhead is held in the bone, if your hand turns around it as you enter the bone, then widen the bone and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be drawn out, if you leave it alone, and then resume the extraction as it is drawn out; and if it is an arrowhead that has been drawn out, and you see blood coming from it, if the head of the arrowpoint enters the hair of the instrument; then draw it out, and if the arrowpoint is hair, draw it out at the end entering the instrument to lighten the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrowhead is lodged, then you must remove the entire shaft or the poison if you can, and then treat the wound as best as you can.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the arrowhead is embedded in the shoulder, belly, or abdomen, and it has prolapsed, and you pull it out, if it comes out; then pull out the vein and nerve, and then extract the arrowhead, and then clean the wound as best as you can; and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the spikes used to treat the arrows resembles the beak of a goose, and it looks like this:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in various forms: large, small, and medium-sized, according to the amount of the shaft.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The form of the pointed nail is similar to that of a sparrow's wing, by being inserted at the tip of the shaft, as shown in this figure.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The forms of the nails for driving and pulling are similar to this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	of veins that are safe to open are XXXI, of which the head is XVI, which means: the two arteries that are after the ears, which are called the "herb" arteries; and the two arteries that are in the two temples appearing; and the vein that is in the front of the head, which is called the "aspirers"; and the vein that is emerged from the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose; and the glands that are on the collar; and the veins that are in the lips of the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and the veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	1. The arteries that are commonly found in each arm are usually five: one is the temporal, and it is located on the left side of the costal groove, and is called the "temple vein"; and the other is the subclavian, and is called the "fasten"; it is composed of the temporal and the basilic, and is called the "basilic vein"; and the basilic is located on the right side of the costal groove, and is called the "abdominal vein"; and the abdominal is located on the left side of the costal groove, and is called the "inguinal vein", and is located under the fascia, and is the one that is found, which opens clearly into the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The saved vein is the one located between the ear and the anus, and if it rains; and in the leg, there are three veins: one is the small vein located behind the pocket of the left costal side, and the second one is the vein called "sepsis," which is located at the ankle of the other costal side; and the vein called "birth" (or "nesse"), which is located in the ankle of the other leg's costal side.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The salvation of the veins located behind the ears helps in childbirth and emigration; and the quality of the salvation, as I said, is that you return to the physician's mouth, and rub the leg where the veins are of a rough cloth; then the physician's collar becomes strained until the veins open at the ears in the dependent part of the cheek: then take the lancet, and cut through the vein just before the bone, then hold your hand firmly on all the veins as you pass, and cut and sew the cloth and the veins as many times as necessary until you see; then tie it and lie down, as long as it is not safe; and I have already said about the incision and the cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The head of the second arteries that are in the second temples, if they are old, diseased, and accustomed to it, and have wetness in the eyes; and if you consider it as I say: and that the patient draws his collar tightly when the veins are open; and it feels cold to your thumb, and then swells; then loosen the knot at the top of the vein on your thumb index, and cut the lancet off, and loosen the vein at the top, and the cloth, as you have done in the other veins, and make sure to draw out the lancet according to your need; then remove the patient's hand from the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it; and then let it form, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken about their comfort and extraction, or beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The first line translates to: "The health of the vein at the front of the face is as good as the health of the cranial vein in ancient facial diseases, migraines, and bruises; and it is distinguished if the patient draws in his neck while twisting, as the eye appears; then take the instrument called 'cautery', which is shaped like this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and firmly hold it with your hand or another object, and let out the blood according to the amount you see; then tell the patient to relax his neck, and keep the eye until it is healthy and never once use a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	1. All that is needed is for the flames to be too close; and it is safe to cross, because the bone is near, and by chance the flames break when they are being tended to.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	2. The safety of the two veins that are in the armor is helpful for the wounds, and the knot, and the bruise, and the pain in the face, and the diseases of the face; and the quality of its safety if it is that the patient draws his neck back twisting any limb, as before; then safe, and so the safety of traversing a little long a little flame wide, because there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, by chance very fierce; then make sure to take enough blood, as much as you can, and then press on the wound, and it will heal well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And if the washing of the vein is not done properly, and it is too cold, and it causes diseases of the face, as well as rashes that come into the face, and even when it is old; and the quality of the washing is such that the herbs stretch out their collars, then press the vein with your left hand, and take a subtle flame and light it on the eyelid that is between the two eyes, because the vein does not open well, and now it will start to bleed; and do not push too hard, and take blood according to your need, then lie down for a night, because it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The patient's health is aided by the application of the cauterizing iron to the wounds at the beginning of surgery and for various diseases such as gout, empyema, corrosion, herpes, and stings; and the quality of the cauterizing iron is estimated if the patient is able to tighten his collarbone on both sides as we have stated; and the master should be present at the head of the patient, and the patient should be placed at a distance widely enough for the surgeon to work freely, without interference from the patient; then another part is treated on the other limb, and the wound is dressed and tightened so that the patient does not strain it; and it is left for the morning, when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the health of the deer
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the lips of the deer helps to close in the mouth, and to prevent the corrosion of the gums, and the cracks in the lips, and the wounds and the pain.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the health is to make the patient stand before you, and tighten his collar as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the teeth, of which one is on the left side and the other on the right, and they are dark because of their black color and their thin black gums: therefore, take one and the other, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, then take the largest of each pair, and all of them, because it is a similar manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the healthy side of the tongue.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	If the healthy side of the tongue is on the side of the throat after the head is healed, and it's at the chin, and there are diseases of the eyes, and diseases of the mouth; and if you can determine which is healthier, if the patient has a black vein in front of your hands before the sun, and feel the tongue, and look at both sides of the throat, then they are healthy on both sides, and do not worry too much, for these are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The usual costly veins that are healthy are found in two ways: either by pressing on the entire flame with a wide finger, or by using a thin olive oil as you would when shaving, and they are called "anesil"; and they are wide and thin according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the fire cautery is such that it is named after the flame, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is suitable for opening the veins that are thick with large clots of blood, and contain large clots and turmoil; and this is the form of the fire cautery:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more subtle in its application, and it is safer for the veins that are thin, or there is thin blood in them:
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The health of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are deosy in the throat, and the collar, and the chest, and the belly; and it is necessary for the physician to make sure it is healthy, and to avoid the artery that is deosy:
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it pricks the artery, and blood comes out, then it should be held steady if it can be, as I have said; and it should not be pinched by fire, but cut if it can be, as I have said.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the boil does not open clearly, then it should be held steady if it can be, and another one should be changed; or you do not want any rain on it, or you want to open the vein with the arm: it will open clearly; and the cautery is applied hot, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you see the vein swelling, and it does not open if you hold the arm steady, and touch the vein as far as you can reach; then sign the vein with your thumb, and then release the arm, and cut the vein with the hot cautery; and be careful not to hurt the artery when you see the vein bulging, because it is the artery: do not cut.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you see coming out from above as the urine of a child, and it is red and subtle, signifying that there is no artery: haste to you, and put your hand far away, then observe your hand when it is free of pain, which many times occurs; hold your arm, let it be, and do not move the patient's joints; and so be cautious, and do not move until it is healthy.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if it is not inflamed, and it hurts, and the physician is not present, then if the artery is open, as it may happen, due to the return of the head; treat it.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a scalpel of fistula, and make it, and take one of the halves and tie it well to the other; if it is not stained, it is well; if not, then the cure, as we have said, with powders that stain blood; and the stains are not much in other positions for the small wound of the wound, and the power of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The health of the vein in the environment if it helps that it treats the wound with blood from the head and chest, because it is composed of basilic and cranial, as we have said; and it is necessary for the physician to relax the nerve that is wounded, and if it does not too much in a short time, and it relaxes the nerve, and it grows and the health is grown, and by chance it cannot heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open any holes for its subtlety, then it is necessary that you heal the instrument first; and hide the nerve from your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is blood between the two veins, if they are long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The treatment of the head is beneficial, if it attracts blood to the chief, and helps the wounds; and it is more helpful in pricking with olive oil or with mercury, because it is the most safe of all wounds, because it does not harm the nerve or the artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Indeed, it is better to use a lighter force, and do not hurt anyone the first time, and continue; and by chance, the legs may be affected in some men, but it does not hurt anyone the first time.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the health depends on your thought.
