When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	Dislocations are caused by no joint of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The first line of the text is translated as: "If the leg ventouses are healthy, it is because they open widely, attracting blood from the entire body, and alleviate old pains from rains, labor, and prostate, and stimulate the flow of blood. They are in the legs of the II sophenes and II chevilles, and all of them weaken the body after long use, and cause headaches in various positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The second line of the text is translated as: "If you are putting in the ventouse first, and then again, and move it gently, and continue doing this until you see the red and swollen leu, and the pain subsides, then stop, and reset the ventouses, and take care in the position of the body, because there are those who have such pain and large wounds: if you only injure once, and make wide wounds, and a few are healed; and gently rub.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	If the patient is thin, then it may be injured twice: the first time by subtly cutting the vein.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	If the patient is very thin, then it may be injured three times: the first time by subtly cutting the vein, and the second time by accidentally cutting it again. However, if we only touch it once, we will not cause any further harm.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	If we remove too much blood, we often return to it; and if the patient is very thin, then it may be injured frequently, and if we cut it deeply, and it is noticed, and those who have thick skin and are firm, that you apply ointments of opening and dissolving essential oils to the wounds: if this is the case, use olive oil, or orange blossom oil, or sunflower seed oil; and if it is silver, use sage oil, or lavender oil, or chamomile oil, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, then take olive oil, or balsam, or oil of anise, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the part to be cleaned is soft and large pores, it is not necessary to put oil on it, but it is recommended to wash it after the extraction of rose water, or cold water, or mushroom water, or violet water, or porcelain water, or any similar substance.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And the one who has moisture on his lips, if he raises his saliva, or rose water, and mint water, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	Those who have excessive superfluity rise from wine vile, or from ague of depression, or from decoction of anet or chamomile, or from other similar causes; and they are not healthier before bathing than after, but rather an hour or two after bathing; and they do not sleep before ventilation, and they must wake and stay awake when they need to ventilate and when they are ventilating.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	If those who are in health are cold and too much and inflamed, it happens that they crave cold things, such as green apples and endives and leafy greens, and similar things; and they drink punches, and char of cheese, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	1. Those who have a cold complexion, if they pregnant honey, and sweet wine odorous, which is between viel and noveil, and drink little, and drink pucins and small oiselz and pigeons; and the hour that it will be wet, if it must more drink than mengier; and it is necessary to give to some men once triaicle or muscate before ventosacion, or after, for to comfort the principal members; and it should be subtle the without, but it only those who are chaut the boivent.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	1. The wounds that are made to hurt are those that are made on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the stomach and the bowels and the bladder and the urethra, for this member does not suffer much hurt outside, and only causes pain when it attracts pain from one part to another, as we do with the mammaries when they are not sick; to overcome viscosity that is in the member, as we make wounds on the stomach and the bowels to sweeten the member; and to relieve pain when it has opulation or incision, if it attracts opulation or incision by chance, or if the incision lacks flesh from its lobe; and it is made empty when it is placed on the liver and the spleen when it has viscosity retained, and these wounds are administered dry to suck them only; and never are they administered together with fire, and never with hot aqua tede, as in diseases that cause much weeping, and in this way we fill the wound with hot water or with herbs cooked in it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the vacuum administered by fire is:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	The form of the vacuum administered by fire is: two palm-wide and half a thumb's width, with a small pertus at each end, like a needle, and it is made of iron or silver, so that it does not cut the patient's skin when inserted into the member; and in the middle, there is a groove of iron or silver to hold a catheter, and they are either large or small according to the disease and age of those who take them, because the vacuums of children are different from those of adults, and the thin ones are different from the fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	1. And it must be placed on the dressing over the member: take the candle or liniment, and put it in the opening of the thread that is in the opening of the thread, so that it is clear at the end of the opening that it does not burn the patient; then place it on the member, and you must be as we have said, if you see that it rises, and if it vaporizes, and then take the liniment as before, and reapply often, if you can.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	1. In the dressing that is in the patient who is sick with catarrh, without any wound or opening, and is not sick except when it is clear with a runny nose, and is placed over the member only when it is, and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	1. Withouts are not stolen except in members where it is not possible to put a ventouse due to their small size, such as the lips and genitals, and similar parts; and in these parts, desnuez of char is done if it is not too long or thin, and other similar things. And when you see withouts that are in soft waters with a nice sensation, take them and put them in a soft water bag as much as they are family-like, and have nothing in the belly; then make the member healthy and clean, and then clean the wound, and put on the withouts when they are red, and then put them on, as long as they are flat and not paining, whether it is the left or right one, if it can be put on with a ventouse, then put it on, for this is after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then raise the leg of the patient, and then the arm; and if the patient is too tired after the operation, then take cold linen and wet it, and wrap around, as long as the limb is not swollen; and if the limb is swollen, then take cold linen or vinegar, or similar things, as long as it is swollen; or take half of the patient's feet that have been pared, and leave them on the foot as long as they are burning, if it becomes firm now; and if you have more experience, then take more pieces of wood.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the wounds do not take on the salve, if you froize the lew of clean water, or you use a needle as much as it needs, and then put them in, and as they feel the clean water, if they heat; and when you see that they are closing, if you put a pinch of aloe and silk or wool, or charcoal, if they close now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	I advise you, my dear friend, that the matter of this chapter will not seem strange to anyone who has read the former books, and who has not; and for this reason, the science has been lost in our land, because I have never found any book on the subject; and I do not know if there is any, except perhaps by the science of the old books, or by my own study and treatment of the science, and by experiment, and by the habit of my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained in it, and I have summarized it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the fractures that have been produced, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say at the beginning of this book the words and chapters or the sage puts his understanding, and moreover, so as to prove it, if those who have experienced it believe and learn this noble art, and they teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture, dislocation, torsion, or twisting occurs to no one, if it comes to pass that you have stronger pain on one side than the other, as weak as a horse's neck, or as fragile as a child's arm; or if you hold it and it is not very tense, or too loose; and if you have cold hands, it means cold juices, and chilled hair, and do not drink cold drinks, nor eat any thin soups, and do not fill your belly with too many meats that fill the veins with blood, as long as you have no doubt of apoplexy or expansion of matter in the member; if the patient's pulse returns to its normal state after using it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	When the bones begin to heal, if it is necessary to feed the patient with foods that cause large viscosity, or if it is thick like dough, such as wheat, rye, barley, pork, fish, wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the more the patient is fed, the faster the fracture heals.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And you advise that fractures of the bones and decrepitudes cannot be well recovered or healed according to their nature by the help of the limbs, nor those who are too flexible, as with the bones of little children; but if it is necessary, first reset the large tendons that have been torn and joined to the member as it was before, and do not delay for long in doing so, and because it is necessary to feed on large quantities of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you know that fractures come in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the skull is different from that of the foot or leg, and I will tell you all kinds of fractures in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes in and another that comes out, like the size of a pen's point to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture at a small notch.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each fracture has its own way and proper instrument in restoration, according to what remembers come into the bone; and it is known that the fracture of the bone is by that which is broken, and open well by defense, and soon by pressure of the hand; and when it is not twisted nor at the tip, and the pain is not great in the shoulder, there is no fracture; but it may have twist, or notch, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you can only manage to move it with your hand, but apply the medicines that will come after, and then gently pull it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And check that the fracture will be in the joint, and the two parts are disjointed, it is now necessary to fix them evenly, unless the wound closes and returns; and if the wound closes and appears, as long as the wound is calmed, then it is left loosely and gently in the place where you can lightly and wisely insert it, and check that the restoration of the part is lighter than the restorations of other bones or pieces; then it is pulled, as it should be done after.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	1. And if in the bone of the foot there are pieces broken, if they are two parts, it is hands or fingers, or in your hand some small limbs, or in two cords, or in one cord and in your hand; and place the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are healed, if you reset by your own means the additions in their places in the muscles that you pull, and keep that by your will not cause the surgeon's injury or pain; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	2. And it feels good in your hand if it seems that it is not well: if it curves beautifully, and is not strained too much, do not press as they who come by their own experience know how to do, with the force of contraction and pressure on the member, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	When the member is in pain, if the patient holds the limb still, neither watching nor sleeping, nor turning, nor otherwise, and ensures that the limb is securely held so that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when there is no pain, if it is not yet at the point of dislocation, and it is necessary to set it in its proper position so that there is no pain; and keep it in place until the time comes when you return it to its original state; and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I will tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	There are different types of broken bones in small, large, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For if it has bitten the limbs, just like a snake and worm: if it comes with folds of fine linen and subtle ones; and those that are large, like a bowstring or rope: if it comes with a wide and hard cord, for the wide ones entangle all the great member, and draw it evenly, unless it has no knot; then it enters light and loose bands, three times or four according to the size of the member, and holds the hand tightly along the entire member, then goes to the end of the fracture and draws it less than the fracture itself, and softens the member a little at a time until you feel a great part of the healthy flesh, then take another member, turn the end towards the broken part, and then return to the part opposite the fracture, and draw it gently, not too hard or too loosely, as we said in the first case; then put between the entangled lips of linen or wool, as it is even, then tie all with a knot, and then put your well-made ties on if it has no knot or slipped.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	If it is inflamed or infected, apply something soothing to the inflamed area that also relieves the pain and leaves no marks. Then tighten your eyes, and they should be of a width of one and a half fingers or less, or of the size of a knuckle, or of the thickness of a palm leaf, and they should be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	However, it is necessary that the piece that is placed on the wound be larger and wider than the others; and should also be longer in length according to the size of the member; then tighten the eyes as you did at the first time, then tie a thread around it just like you did in the first time, but do not make it too tight; the more stretched it is, the less it should be; and the thread should be smooth, neither too thick nor too thin, and should be of linen; for if the thread is too thick, as I have seen the works of fools who make their laces with threads of linen, it can cause great errors, because the thread cannot be even if it is too fine, and it only serves to make the eye smaller between each one.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	When the patient is cauterized by the fire, and the hairs are cut long and even, if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the forceps, and the edges are torn, I will tell you the treatment for this afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And it is important not to strain too much on the joints, as all the limbs will be broken in the first place.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not advisable to put on the forceps immediately, but rather after V years or VII, or according to your strength of aposteme chaut; and the way of the ancient emplaustres to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and that you take flour that is made in the mills, and knead it with much water, and make this dough, not too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of the emplaustre restoring fracture in other positions, as well as for women and young children, because it is neither too tight nor too loose.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	1. Another way to mend breaks and dislocations and twists: take barley, linen, and unguent of myrrh, Arabian gum, and resin; mercury, VIII grains; and make powder, and mix with wool of urine; if the complexion of the face is hot, use this plaster as it is of good composition, and rests the broken bones firmly, and is beneficial to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	1. Another way to mend twists: take resin and mugate, VIIIII grains; mercury, IX grains; arsenic, X grains; and bole, VI grains; cook well, and mix with vinegar or urine of wool, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Other methods of dressing joints and bones, and alleviating pain, and reducing swelling, and fractures: take new cloths, and the oil and butter cooked, and put them on the leg.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore health, but they are good for alleviating the pain of inflammation, and properly treating fractures.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Other methods of plaster that restore broken bones: take dry fig leaves, and earth oven leaves, and burn them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Other methods of plaster for restoring bone fractures and reducing inflammation: take fresh leaves of fig, and earth oven leaves, and burn them together, and make a plaster.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	1. Gather the roots of mallow, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of violets, and each part; and boil, and strain with wine, and cleanse your limbs with wet or dry coriander or sage, or any other herb, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	1. Another way to make the plaster more effective when the wound is deep and comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	1. Gather the roots of mallow, linseed meal, balm, honey, and salt, and each part; boil, and marinate with wet or sweet vinegar, or wine, according to the choler of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras says in his book that nothing should be put on the broken bone to restore it, only wax and oil, and nothing more, and he says it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	It seems that Galen says that things should be put on the broken bone to restore it, such as dry hot things like mustard and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to show what is good for a wound and pain: take mouse and chew the tail or the tail of an owl, or the hair of a fox, and wrap it around, and the nail, and then make an application and apply it to the limb.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the swelling will disappear after a short while, and take care not to cause pain or discomfort in the patient's joints; if it does not disappear by hand pressure, and pain comes to the joint, or itching, or tenderness, if you hurry and remove it, and cleanse the wound with the plaster now, and gently dampen a cloth, and dip it in cool water, and lift the limb as much as the itching ceases and the pain subsides, then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on a dry cloth, gently moisten with cool or rose oil, and tie it with a knot, until you are sure of no aposteme, and allow the inflammation in the limb to subside, and the pain to cease, then resume the application of the plaster gently, and a little emplaustre, and do not strain it too much; and gradually as it becomes healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	When you see that the wound is bleeding, having bruises and pain, and swelling is all over, and you have the skill to plaster and bandage, if it happens again, as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	When you do not see any sign of the wound closing within three days, four days, or seven days, and never more than twenty days, according to what we have seen, as soon as the break opens and approaches the bone, then the restraint is greater than before, and the flesh enlarges, as I have said before; and if you see the wound drying up more than it should, be careful that no diseases come; take the heat of the fire, every time you clean it, and do it once a day, and keep the water in a pot; through this treatment, you will cut off the diseases from the wound, and mend the harm caused by the flesh: this is good, and if it does not heal within a week, and I have nothing else to offer than pain and improper care.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various kinds of wounds
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many kinds of wounds, and various forms; for there are wounds made by the impact of the spear, and which pierce the bone completely, as if it were cut with a knife or sword; and therefore this kind of wound is called "piercing" wound.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	The spear pierces the bone through different senses, and this kind of wound is called "absolute" wound; and these are the wounds of these two large or small gashes.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it has an impact that is embedded, or a cut or piercing, or a pricking on the edge of the piercing, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	If there is a persistent fracture, which approaches the skin that is loose from the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound or large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	If there is a healing wound that is as subtle as a hair's breadth and is a small cut, and for this it is called the "capillary fracture"; and if the wound that is made by injury, or by piercing, or by seeming thing, and causes the piece of the bone to enter, and is the same as the hot iron when they heated the burners; if it enters the pierced hole.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And there are more cases of those who have moist bones, just like that of children; and they occur in all these ways of fracture that are lightly broken if like these; and I will speak about this in his language.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let's know all ways of fractures by the removal they have, and the inquiry has tried, and by the corrupted char that is had.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary appearance is known by this that when one has discovered the bone, and one scratches around it, if the dark fracture is open.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure of the fracture, keep in mind as many accidents can happen to the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of cole, and admission of understanding, and extension, and numbness, and fever, and the eyes itch and redden, and other signs in more dispositions, if it cannot be cured with doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you do not see a sudden accident, and you hope for a quick recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the pain comes first to you, and it is in the rib, then it is necessary to apply oil before the fourteenth day of the mouse, as you should.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	If it is in this way, then if you apply oil before the ninth day of the mouse, and the skin of the bone is not broken, and the accident that we have mentioned comes, it is necessary to stop.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	If the break of the bone comes at the skin that covers the eye, and it is necessary to cut off the broken part: and if you press the nose of the surgeon's hand on the bone in all the ways you can, and on the figure of the wound more than you can, and when the blood comes out to reveal the bone, or the pus pimple, if it helps that it comes, and when the plague is calmed and secured, then fill the wound with oil-softened flax; and let the plague be calmed and secured for as long as the pus pimple is calmed and secured, and then begin to heal the bone, and it is done according to two ways of incision: one way is that you cut at the narrow end, and it is the form.
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	Then he cuts another piece of greater size than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is if you have many different sizes, some are narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and they are made of iron; and carved lightly so as not to pierce the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and thick, it comes to pass that you perforate it easily, otherwise you must administer pieces with tareers, and do not make them too large so as not to go beyond the end of the bone, and they must have a margin or a circle that does not let the point go beyond the bone; and you must have more pieces, if each one fits in its socket for the size of the bone, if you have tareers for each test; and this is the form of the three methods of tareers:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	1. The quality to perceive the broken bone is that you place your thumb on the bone, and turn it around until you feel that the bone is perceived; then put your thumb on another part a little later, and then do everything around it, then cut as the incisions in the bone that is between the holes, and do it more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, whenever you touch the skull with your hand, or any of the splints that you have like needles, pincers; and make sure you do not touch the brain or the face.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have perceived and cut the bone, if the wound that is made in the bone by another instrument resembling an incision covers the whole bone, but it should be more delicate and subtle than the other incision; and if it does not cut any small bones, nor any scales, if the light bones are gently pressed on the splints; then cure the wound with tentes and ointments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of cutting is when it is said that the Gaulish method is better, which is more certain; and the most powerful, and this is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to remove a part of the bone, where the fracture opening is wide, if you will then measure from the center of this incision, and the shape of the lens-shaped hole will be:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut too much, and the part that is taken is in two parts if the cutting is towards the bone; then, with a small hook, if you lightly cover the entire bone, and be careful of the thread that is left behind; if it is close to the bone, for the bone is easily felt, and causes pain.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce through the skin, and the bone is only cracked, and it has small pieces, then cover it with a soft file (raser subtil) that you have several quantities of, to smooth out each part of the bone according to its size and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you go before with a rough file, and after with a more subtle one, and keep doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In every other hair removal and subtle fracture, it is necessary to adjust according to its address; and this is something that cannot be undone for the one who has studied in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	1. If the wound is discovered, then it comes to pass that you put on linen bandages according to the size of the wound, and olive oil, and place it over the wound; then take another bandage doubled in two or three, and olive oil and olive oil, and place it over the first bandage; and do this more lightly than you please, so that you do not burn the linen, then apply other linen bands, and do not strain it too much, only as much as the wound allows; and leave it on for one or two days, until the sore is calmed, then remove it, and apply medicines such as raisins, flour, powder of incense, and aristocratic herbs, and similar things; and from these things make powder, and place it over the wound, and apply further medicines without biting; and let the wound be clean, so that you do not leave the ointment or assemble bowels, for if bowels are assembled under the skin, they can cause great harm to the patient; for if something mouth-biting is placed on the wound, it causes great pain to the surgeon.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	If nothing happens unexpectedly to the patient, if no accidents come to the helper, as we have said, then there is doubt in the matter.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blacking does not come from the medicine we have put on, then some virtue has, if you take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and one part of glue, and put it on your face; then the cure is done in the ways of cures that it covers, as long as it is healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	It is said that the two parts of the nose are never broken, unless one only, for they are bones; and this is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it is bent or twisted, and then it becomes healthy.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should cut off your small finger or thumb, and make the break even with the nail of your index finger, and in the pouch as long as it does not resemble its natural figure; and do this lightly, and warn that the patient does not feel pain through your touch.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part of the nail, and cannot be reached by the thumb, then you should put it even with the end of a large ring.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in the second part, then you should repeat the first joint, and if not, after the ninth or tenth day, when the swelling has subsided, then cut off the tip of the nail with a sharp knife, if the break is in a part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you cut into another part, the wound is; and let the tentacles be as large as they fill the cavities with pus.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And no restorer will say that one must smooth the tentacles in burr, and each year.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It seems to me that this is well, but they must be smoothed in the making of beef flour and milling powder; then leave the tentacle, as long as the bone is firm, and the cartilage is hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And no time do you cut on the neck of tents, and if it is soft and hanging, and holds the breastplate, and blows the salve among; or as you have seen.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	When the abscess is incised and the pus comes out during the operation, if you use a piece of cloth or cotton wool dipped in rose oil or in a drop of laundry soap.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess does not come out, if you use ointment made from flour of Sisam and incense powder, mixed with eggs, then cover it with light sponge pieces, and do not sew the wound; and if the wound in the nose is small, and it is torn into small pieces, if the sutures are easy to remove at this time, then cut the suture, and treat the scars as scars, and solder them with lead, if they are suitable for this; and if there is no scar on the wound, if you treat it with bandages, and insert needles, as long as it is healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	The first line of the text to translate is: "de la routure de la mandibule".
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is dislocated, there is no wound, and the fracture is slight only, and it does not become two pieces, but rather a single piece, and it is not broken in two, but rather bent slightly, if one knows how to do it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the left part, to place your index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left mandible, then place your index finger on the right hand, and gently bend the fracture, and hold it with the other hand, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the lower jaw is described as two, then it comes that you apply an extension of two parts, as it should be equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth move or break, or there is a fracture of a gold or silver thread, then they are attached to the broken lower jawbone with a double-layered cord; and a heavy stone or piece of leather is placed along and wide according to the size of the jawbone, and it is tied to the mouth that you use, and the surgeon orders the patient to rest, and feeds light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, if it is delayed for three days, and then returns to where it was; and it is plastered with flour from a flour mill with a large amount of urine or flour from sinew, after which the broken lower jawbone is stepped on; and it is plastered with a lighter plaster, and it sticks to the mouth and does not change its position, as long as it is healthy, many times it is healthy in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if the wound becomes infected, then we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and multiple wounds, a small piece of bone may be exposed; if the bone is subtle and can be easily covered.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is wide, then enlarge it according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have all the bones in place and there is no lack, if the wound is large, then put the stitches together according to your need; until it is healthy.
de la forcele	of strength.

The forceful break occurs multiple times in front, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is in three ways: either it is broken and dislocated in two, and it has pieces, and it is the lighter one to restore; or it is a fracture with wound.

And the dislocation is when the fracture is in pain, that you have two assistants, if some paint the helper that feels the forceful break; and the others extend the collar towards the part; then set the fracture in your two hands, so that it forms as it should, and there should be no appearance or movement.

et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it seems like a spoon, and is not too thick, and should be as wide as you want, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the will; and there are two heads, if you see, and some are large, and others are narrow, if it is the swelling of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of aposteme chaut, if the wound is large, or you doubt aposteme chaut, if you use the wound with drapelz and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if you prick your finger with a hot iron, if it does not bleed much, apply some oil of rose and almond, and wrap it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And if you dislocate your shoulder with a hot iron, if it does not bleed much, apply some oil of rose and almond, and wrap it. de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement. de la brisure dou pis	of the break
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is never broken in its environment, but this sometimes happens; but it often breaks in the heat.

de la brisure des costes	Of the breast fracture
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois. de la brisure dou col	Of the break of the shoulder

de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the fracture of the bone of the shoulder

When you have made it even, if you put on the plaster, then put on a piece of flax or wool, and tighten the fracture, if it does not move; and apply the leather to the ribs, as long as the swelling is equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if you have a fever and come, if it does not hurt, as long as the fever is calm, and put on what we have mentioned before; and then return to the restoration, and tighten it as it should be, if there are no other accidents; and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the shoulder dislocation
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is the bone that is between the upper arm bone and the shoulder blade of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then it must be reset according to one of two methods: one of which is to use a flat piece of wood with rough edges, as shown in this figure:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient. When the shoulder is dislocated and it comes out, if it is not strained for at least seven days, and it is lubricated with oil and ointment on both sides, as long as the shoulder is dislocated; then it is strained, and the manner of straining if you place the plaster on the break, then assemble the arm with the auxiliary, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and tie it, and strain with the auxiliary and with the arm, so that the arm is in its place, nothing should hinder it, or if the bone does not move.

When you doubt that the bone does not move, use these and place a wider and stronger nail on each, with two spaces between them, so that each nail is as large as it passes through three parts of one; then draw the nails tighter, as I said at the beginning of this chapter, more firmly and less by moving them away.

de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "humerus" and the "ulna", and one of them is smaller and is located in the pocket; and the other is larger and is located in the little humerus; by chance, only the large humerus or the small one is broken, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is light and the cure; but when the large ones are broken, if it is a poor cure, and more painful than when they were broken individually.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bones that are broken, then it is best to extend lightly and equalize them.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bones, then they should be stretched more forcefully; and extend it over the thumb, and lift the palm of the hand higher than the other, and the toes should be lower than the others, and the patient's weight should be on his own foot, and some other parts on the opposite side. Then extend the joints of the arm to the part opposite the hand, either to the little finger or to another part on the opposite side.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he puts it in place as best as he can.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is in pieces, then he puts each piece in its place, and if there are no loose parts that point to the bone, and you cannot restore it in its place, then as we have said before, set it and the bone.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken to the individual surgeon; if he takes care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of restoration, there are abscesses that open, if the dressing made of rose oil and waxy clay is not too hard or too stiff, and it is gently wrapped around, as long as the abscesses are calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then the bone, and he puts the template of the powder with a lot of urine, with the sticks, so that the sticks are wider than the others; and he checks if there are VI sticks or arms in more positions: whether the break is in one of the bones, or in two; and it is tightened more under the break than other parts, and less by moving away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and the wounds that are under the break, which are moist and slippery, should not be too hard or sharp; and the strings, which are drawn, should be of linen, not too long or short, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the limb after some time.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any accidents come to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, if you heat the member with hot water until the itching is calmed; and let the member rest without being tightened.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the stretching, and if the limbs are smoothed and the bones are exposed, and it seems like something, then it is done.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the knots cannot come to the member because it is too tight, since it comes to the member; if you smooth it in your hands, and let some time pass, until the knots are loosened and then stretched.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	If these things do not come to the patient within twenty years.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If the dislocation is entred, then the hands can be placed on his collarbone, and it should be equal; and there should be no movement or deformation, and he should sleep on his back; and it is hoped that this dislocation is restored in XXX years or XXXV, and by chance in XX years, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the dislocation of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Wishes that on the back of the hand and as we have two come few dislocations, and only pain many times.

Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is at the sides of the abdomen of the plant, then make a sleeve of drapes, and instruct the patient to tie it to his broken plant; then stretch from a long drape, and make the splint as large as the plant of the hand, and tighten it, if it is necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	If the fracture is at the elbow, if you manage to place a splint on it, and another on the forearm, if the hand is over the elbow and straight, then the arm will be completely fixed between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the fracture does not involve both arms, if they are equal, then it should be fixed; and with the forearm, if you see that a splint is placed right and small to fix the fracture, and it does not move; and if the fracture is in other parts, such as the index finger or another, if it is equal, and the hand is lifted with the healthy one, or if you tie them together, as much as possible, or if you place a splint, as I have said; and take care in restoration and position of the abscess, and cut off what comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken cheek
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the cheek is often broken, and it can be seen when it turns forward and backward; the restoration is done by tying the ligatures of the fracture, and the other is left alone.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient groans at their face, then extends each muscle of his limb to its equal part; and it is when the fracture is healed.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is approaching the root of the cheek, then one or more of the ligaments are pulled towards the puncture, and the others are left alone.

It is necessary that you wrap the knee with a bandage made of the first doubling to the third or fourth, and remove any excess, then bend the leg until the heel reaches the root of the nail, and place the long fil between the thigh and the leg, loosening the knee joint; then bend the leg and the thigh with the bandage, then put the brace on, and place an estile on the bone of the leg; then use the leather between the leg and the thigh to make the strap tighter, then begin to tie the third or fourth turns on the brace; and as more parts of the brace you use, and less the strap is tightened; then take out the three turns of the fil that you have tied between the leg and the thigh, and the three estiles that are located there, then return to the knee joint of the chief of the fil, until you see the patella; the strap, if it does not move from its place, then let it alone, then leave it, then it will not apostime or swell or any other sign.
