And if it happens, if he lets it go, and addresses what comes, as we have said many times; and if it has pieces of bone that prick, if he can, then it is possible; and if not, then it comes to cut the leg, and draw out the splinter; and the cure, as we have said, depending on how healthy it is.

de la ruelle dou genoil	Of the galley's gall

de la brisure de la jambe	Of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. It is said that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called "true" by right, not "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile". And it happens all the same as with the arm, and for this the restoration is done in the same way as with the arm properly. And if both bones are broken together, then turn the leg around all parts.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, then turn forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bones are broken, then it is felt with great pain, and it is seen that it is well; then turn slowly.

de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the break of the bones of the shoulder
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	The ankle does not have a break, but the bones of the shoulder never break and must be very strong, and they only wear out in more positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if the bones of the shoulder break and you see these bones pushing over each other, if you put your hand on the ground, it will be very painful like frost, just like when you fly, then put your hand on the shoulder, and lift the bone as much as it comes out in its place; then press it with the thumb and thumb nails, and cut off a small table at the top of the shoulder blade, then draw it towards the shoulder, then wrap the cloth around your hand, and other things that you know.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, if the bone is not healed, you will find the bones uneven, broken, dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are two fractures, if they are repaired, as we have said, then put a splint on the other one according to the length of the bone; and make it larger at the end, then make a support for that joint as we have described, and tighten the strap; and if there are two or three or more fractures, if you put one on each, according to its quantity, wrapped in one layer of linen, and tighten the strap around the pike of the joint; and make sure it is hanging down from the top of the pike so that it covers well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	It is necessary that you do not overlook the other things I have said in other breaks, as we have said; and attend to each accident as it occurs.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the bone fracture of the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the woman's bone is broken, if it is set in place, then it leaned towards the side of the wrist, and was held by the hand; then the seam of the nature of the malaide was filled with cloth, and it was placed as large as I have shown; then the woman was opened, and the back was gently lifted a little at a time, and then the coton was jumped, as soon as it came to the entrance of the nature, and the bone was returned with the sto; and if she saw pissier, if the coton was pissier, and if she pisseit, she was re-seamed, and in seven days or more: if the fracture is restored, and if you see it, take a bowl of berbis, and tie it to the pertus with a cainne, and blow all the bowl into the nature; then let the cainne form, as long as the bowl is empty: the nature will return to the fracture; then fill it with cloth, and leave it for no more than days, until it is healthy.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	When the bone of the arm is broken, or of the woman, if it is restored as we have said in the bone of the cheek; and these breaks are not hidden that closely to the one who sets the study and the use, and understands my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break means in more positions the right way of restoration: understand the direction.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the shoulder, when it is broken, take an owl's grip and bite the shoulder; then wrap around drapes, and leave it three turns or in the opposite direction, and it will be quickly cured.
de brisure avec plaie	Of a fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with wound, just as it is large, if it is like the bone of the shoulder or elbow, or seeming, that he be now healthy, if the wounds that we have mentioned testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the healthy wound is, if the inflammation of vitrol, if you have nothing else, then resume to restore the fracture in the same hour, or the next day, if the patient does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the patient does not come the next day, leave the restoration until the next day, as long as the inflammation is calmed, and do not touch it again on the third or fourth day, because you will cause the patient to come with an unwanted accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone is broken, it should be set as gently as possible at the end of the knee, with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not easy to put in your hands, if the splint is made of iron, seven or eight times as long as the bone, and the size according to the size of the wound; and for this, it is necessary to make three or four, according to how many there are in each case of fracture; and so it should be firm but not too heavy, so that it does not slip during compression of the member in your hand, and should be also in front, and large at the front end.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And is called "lance", because it is to place the heads of the bones on the head of the bone; and the bore once, as much as it rises, and let them meet each other equally.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is not noticeable, and the fragments cannot well grasp the bone, then it comes that you cover the head of the bone with your hand as much as the fragments have power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you do not manage to bring the bone back, as we have said, if you cover it with an instrument that is suitable for your hand, or sharp or thin, then relieve this which is difficult in the bone of roughness and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	When the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, it is important to check if there is any malalignment in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you keep it in its natural position for a while, then apply a piece of black vinyl tape that is clean and not oily, to avoid infection and decay; then administer the medication as soon as you have reset the bone, and leave the wound open, covering it with a sterile bandage according to the size of the wound, and be sure that the wound does not become strained with the fracture; and many times it has been found that the patient's leg has improved, and they have come back to see the doctor or died or corroded never; and the stitches are more slippery and slippery than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	When the wound is large or severe, and you doubt that you will arrive in time, as we have said, and you feel pain in the leg, but there is no way to put on stockings; then wrap the leg in cloth, draping it tightly, and tie it.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	When you see after the first or second day that the wound has healed, and if everything has been treated with it, and you have a remedy for painful wounds, which is a powerful ointment and similar to this.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	It is necessary that you free the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, as long as it is swollen and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	It is necessary that the limb be aligned in a certain way that the belly is not affected lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If they persist, and it cannot be held back but causes the belly to move, it has small pieces of bone, and it is necessary that you wrap the wound with a bandage, and all these pieces cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	If a fistula comes to the joint, or any other form of corruption, and it is necessary that you treat it, according to what is said in this chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	If the bone is broken and exposed through the limb, as if it were the bone of the knee or shoulder, and other similar bones of large limbs, if it is not set, because often death follows, but it leaves it until it bleeds; by chance, it may be cured after 20 or 30 years, then treat the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Of the bones that come out of the cold
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We come many times after the cold, and at the same time when it is near the joint, and it is a matter to see how it looks like a limb; and by chance it cannot make the limbs its own nature.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If the cold has not affected it: if it is managed with warming medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolle, and other similar things, and you do not take any of these things or all together, and mix them with warm stomach or with an excess of beer or with honey; and they are placed in baths, and drawn well, and not slipped from the hands; and then they are loosened, and another is taken again, as long as the nodations are ostee; or if you draw a piece of well-made plaster; for the property of the plaster is that it all cures the swelling of the members; and when the nodation is already converted into hardness like a piere, and it is sore of the oster, if the raseur is made, and the superfluity is apparent; or you let it rest on any other part, as long as it is ostee, and the cure as long as it is sane.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	A weak limb that is after the injury
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and weakened after the weak limbs and subtle, if there are causes: either it is because it was too tightly bound, and not as it should have been; or because it got too many stitches, and could not come to the member; or due to a multitude of inflammation; or because there were too many movements, not in its time; or because it had little blood in its body, and was weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is if you make the patient lie down on his back and tighten the cloth around him as much as possible until he does not multiply it in himself; then give him a bath, and then joy and relief; then put something on the member, if it attracts great inflammation, and often the inflammation is due to heat, until the inflammation reaches the member; and relieve it to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	A dislocated limb after the joint has moved out of its place.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is swollen after realignment, and the bones are fractured open, and the dislocated form of the limb is deformed, it is not in its natural state: if one does not believe the folk who say that the bone must be broken all at once, and many others have done this in our land; and these parts are blamed, and great harm comes from it, and by chance the death occurs; however, if the wounds and tortures are fresh, and it is necessary to cleanse them with hot water or herbs that are cooked, like willows, and roots, and honey, and similar things; and I apply a mollifying ointment, as well as dyaquilon well made, and take the vismalve muscle and cook it with melted butter or olive oil, and apply it thus; or take fat figs and roast them with finely ground colon, and similar medicines that dry the sweat.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And no time is there where the node does not continue to rub continuously and long with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be a movement in the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is awakened and hardened, like a wound, and there is need for the healer to cut, then it comes to cover the bone, with a subtle and light incision; and put on bandages and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to none, if it now comes to bring sense to the target.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if we are late, if we read it, and by chance if we reset it on the shoulder; because we cannot move it to the ear where it is swollen: many times come pain and other pains; always, when this happens, I make the patient healthier, then leave it, as long as the fever is calmed; then heat and oil are applied to the limb, then reset it gently, and cure each member as we have cured it in its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	I have ordered the cauteries for the dislocations of the shoulder joints.
des mandibules	for the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	There are times when the mandibles are dislocated, and the dislocations of the jaws are in two ways: either they are a small piece of their bones, and are softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, and hang downwards, and close the mouth, and cannot hold the saliva in the mouth, and cannot close the mouth, and wrap around the tongue with the speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	If the dislocation is small, it returns through more positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	When it is complete and accomplished, if you reset it as quickly as possible, without force; and in such a way that the patient's hands mark the surgeon's, and cut the skin of one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the mandible, which is of the second part; and the other two hands are deformed to make them equal; and command the patient to smooth and move his jaws, and all parts.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the patient should be aligned as it should be in its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the patient is reset, it should be done with gentle force, that is, the mandibles are assembled, as long as the hot and oily eyes are applied, until they are reset lightly; do not force the patient to reset, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	When they are properly aligned and the patient's mouth feels relaxed, if you put soft cloths on the cheek made of olive oil and wax, then lightly tie them with strings; let the patient sleep on his back, and his head should be between two pillows so that he does not move to the right or left, nor strain himself to breathe, but eat light food as long as the pain is steady and does not affect the jawbones; then take what you see and do not force open the mouth with the tongue and drink, as long as the jawbone is well relieved and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	When the lower jaws cannot be set in place within an hour and are not converted to their proper position, if fever and chills come on, and by chance a solution of stomach, and by chance vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, you will know that it is disastrous; and many have died in nine years.
de la forcelle	from force
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The force cannot be removed from the cost of continuing the bone and the hip, and it is always dislocated at the end, and that is felt by everyone.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is if the patient is able to stand on his own two feet and extend his arms; then press the head against your palm, and it will return; then place the splint and bandage on it, and tighten it; and the one who is facing the shoulder cannot be dislocated; if not, and if it is not dislocated at any time, then reset it on the shoulder, as we have said; then place the splint and bandage on it, and tighten it, and command the patient to rest as soon as he is healthy; and then realign the chest bones, when the patient is able to bear the weight of his limbs.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three ways the shoulder can dislocate: either it dislocates at the shoulder socket; or it dislocates at the upper arm; or it dislocates at the elbow, which is rare; and it does not dislocate from the shoulder blade, nor from the nerves; and more often it dislocates towards the shoulder socket, especially for those who have little strength, because they jump very high; for those who have enough strength, they jump a little, and return a little.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance some men hit or crush the shoulder, and the muscle swells up from an abscess, and make sure it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is therefore necessary that you examine it, as long as you are certain; and then begin the treatment.

And the signs of him who came to the rear, if it cannot expand his genital area, and does not double, and that leg is more tortured than the other, and the anus is softened, and the head of the shoulder is raised against the costal cartilage.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the case of a fresh dislocation, and there are four ways of dislocation, if you hurry to return the joint, and it becomes bent and deformed, and the limb is drawn to the side; by chance if it returns, and there is no other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this way, and you must use strong force to straighten the leg, and bend it with two hands or with the other leg that is placed against the patient's thigh; and others use their hand in a similar way to pull their hands away from the joints, then stretch the leg over the thigh; and some tie the head of the shoulder to the thigh; and extend both at once as long as the patient is lifted off the ground and held still.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is so common as IV appearances, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If this is not the case, then it is necessary to apply treatment to the appearance If the dislocation occurs in the jaw, then it is necessary to seize the patient's shoulder on its healthy side, then tie the bandage on the root of the tooth, and the other limb that is loose, then tie the bandage towards the angle and away from the force; then apply a few more ministrations to the patient's arms, and wrap the large limb of the malpositioned jaw, and extend it according to the form: if it returns to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	When you do not hold the shoulder in this manner as we have said, if it comes to it that you stretch the two feet of the patient's leg together with a strong tie on the two ankles, and on the two thighs, and so the patient's leg is extended twice as much as the others; then hang it from the head of a post, and place the two arms on the ground; then order the minister to embrace the head of the arm, and other ministers hanging with the patient, who embrace form the arm, because the joint returns now in its proper place.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	When the dislocation is at its full extent, if it is gripped by the patient, as we have said in the case of those who have been practiced, and draws the tie on the leg of the injured person properly, and on the foot also; then tie the strips, the head and the other at the ankle, then place the strip between the thighs of the patient in the shape of a bow; and make it wet with drapes so that it does not hurt the patient, then extend each minister towards him, and the patient places it evenly in his hand, and holds the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place the table as we have said in the gilbositeit, and press it according to what we have mentioned for the well-being of the patient.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, if it comes to extend the painful leg with assistance, and as I have said; then place the hand on the painful joint, press with the other hand, and pull back towards the genitalia.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in the groin, and it cannot be extended with assistance, do not lift it from the ground, but it should be as if it was extended in the groin, as we have said on the hips; and place it on your face, and extend it so that it is as we have said before, and it must press on the joint of the table; and it will be when the leg is extended, and they will be equal; then adjust the knees, and put the splint, and hold with a bandage, if the leg does not move; and rest for three or four hours, then remove the splint, and see if they are equal, if the bandage, as we have said before, and leave it for three or four hours, then remove the bandage, and let the member go forward as far as it is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder is dislocated in three ways: it should not be pulled backwards or forward, but only lifted.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	If you command the patient to bend their knee towards their hip, and their heel does not move towards their hip, it indicates that the shoulder is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is if you make the patient lie straight, and extend the leg if possible, and put your back against their knee, and place their foot on their thighs; then take their shoulder with your hands, and stretch between your two fingers, and bend the two joints of the dislocated shoulder; and other means extend the knee, until the shoulder returns to its socket, and the signs are that the leg is gently held by the hip; and apply plaster, and make the leg aerate at the hip, and the fingers assemble firmly three or four times, then remove it; and do not cause the patient to move their limbs too much until the shoulder is comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limbs do not respond, if there is no improvement with massage, as we have said in the treatment of the hemorrhoid, until it is healthy.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the big toe
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The big toe is never used, and it is never completely dislocated, and it is often bent.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the sign that the ankle is dislocated is when it is bent, and before reaching the part where it is dislocated: the hands should be light, and it should be gently extended when it is only weak.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when the ankle is completely dislocated, before reaching the part where it is dislocated: the hands should be light, and it should be gently extended when it is only weak. Then sit down on the patient's right side, and use your left hand to hold the knee; then pull the leg with your right hand, and then with your left hand, and then twice, and then raise it up, and hold it well at the top of the foot; and do this twice, as we have said, by bending and raising the foot; if it returns, that's good; if not, if it does not return, continue the treatment, because it will return; and if it still cannot return, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and hold his ankle firmly on the ground with his hand, and make him lie down with his back against the ground between his knees, and do not let the ankle bleed; then mark the ministers with the ankle, and extend other ministers to the patient's hands or to the leg where the ankle is dislocated; then extend them equally, and the passel should be either between the ankle bones to hold the ankle when it is extended; then put the dislocation in your hands, and mark the healthy leg on the opposite side, and the dislocation will return suddenly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	When it reaches the point, if he applies plaster and covers it, and forms the bandage, and wraps it around the leg, and covers the nerves that are at the ankle joint, where the ligaments are not too tight; then he leaves it on for II to III days, and if the ligaments relax, he tightens it again; then he removes it after III or IV days, and applies a poultice for IV days; and if it does not improve by this time, it is a sign that it has not yet healed.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess forms, it comes, and it is necessary to ease it, as we have said elsewhere, as long as it is healthy.
des dois	The first sentence to translate is: 
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, if they can be extended well in work, and it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in no way uneven or crooked, if you can make the patient lie on their back or side, and place your foot on the opposite hip, then press on the joints with your foot, as it returns; and when it is equal, and there are no gaps, if you place a table at the shoulder and the foot, then form the shape and let go, and rest, until it is healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and it is seen to be restored, often the patient dies: if you are not presumptuous in the cure, whether you are skilled in the art and have not used it long, or whether you are pitiful and merciful and tardy, do not be hard-hearted; and at the beginning of things, appease the inflammation with cooling remedies, and leave the patient in the hands of God, if you see no hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to the bone, unless the inflammation and pain increase; and when the limb is at the bone, if the wound is cleaned and dressed, and the pain is eased, as it should be in simple diseases, and the bones are fractured, and the pieces are small, if the bones break, follow what we have said in simple diseases; and do not enter into a state of despair, according to what we have said, for this is according to your Creator's will, and for the knowledge of your soul and body.
